Fengtian
Regionalist Sentiment
Our government's national goals have always clashed with more localised regionalist messages, which hold greater appeal among the broadly apolitical majority than high-minded republican ideals. Although Zhang Zuolin once rode regionalist sentiment to his current position as ruler, it now threatens to derail his plans to again go south of the Great Wall, conquer Beijing, and reclaim all of China.
Regionalist Resentment
Triggered by rumours, anger simmers quietly in some portions of the public, while others have begun to take to the streets in protest.
Regionalist Outrage
The government's attempts to suppress the so-called 'Dongbei Party' have, at least temporarily, backfired as protests have rapidly evolved into riots in some urban centres. The violence is not yet extreme, but it doesn't need to be. The government now has the justification it needs to crack down and suppress this subversive movement once and for all.
Backward Industry
While Fengtian may contain the second largest industrial base in East Asia, its size conceals obsolete machinery, inefficient practices, and severe mismanagement. Only extensive reforms, backed by a great deal of investment can overcome these challenges.
Divided Governance
Despite its claims to the contrary, the Fengtian Government is plagued by endemic corruption, infighting, and abuse of power. While this is nothing out of the ordinary for China, it impedes the proper functioning of government and limits support for the regime. Should any of the governing factions gain too much influence, disastrous consequences are sure to follow.
Investment Dearth
The economic collapse that followed Fengtian's entry into the last Zhifeng War severely damaged its fiscal base and financial credibility, leaving the government with few creditors, and private businesses with severely limited options. Few have the confidence to invest in Fengtian, either at home or abroad.
Limited Investment
Thanks to government incentives investment has grown, but there is still an overall shortage. We must look to other sources to provide the funds we need.
Intelligence Leak
Through gross incompetence, or even more questionable reasons, a minister has leaked vital intelligence to Fengtian's enemies.
The Year of Righteous Effort
With the Grand Marshal's Proclamation, the nation is united in a strenuous effort to prepare for the rigours of war.
Japanese Aid Cut
Japan has cut all aid to the government as a means of punishment for what it sees as insubordination.
Buying Silver
Silver, by definition, is expensive and the government is presently buying a great deal of it. Once the reserve is full, however, it will have a reliable basis for currency and credit.
Central Bank Collapse
The Central Bank seems to have misplaced millions of taels worth of silver precisely as Japanese banks called for their loans to be repaid. How could this have happened?
The Kwantung Army
The Kwantung Army has been in Manchuria for decades, but their crucial role during Guo Songling's revolt in 1925 gave all the leverage they needed to move their headquarters to Shenyang, greatly increasing their influence over the government. Now they operate as a de-facto military mission and occupational force, protecting the railroads, providing material aid, and giving 'advice'. Unfortunately, ignoring this advice can have dire consequences.
Educational Vacuum
The sudden absence of certain teachers, professors, and scientists has left a troublesome educational vacuum. Foreign and domestic replacements can be found, but at a cost, and not without great inconvenience.
Post-Colonial Chaos
Even at its most limited, Mantetsu's grip on Fengtian's economy and infrastructure was tight, and now as its carefully laid systems and structures collapse, the country as a whole is crippled. It will take time to rebuild and reorganise, but if Mantetsu's influence was greater, it could have been far worse.
Post-Colonial Chaos
Mantetsu's grip on Fengtian's politics, economy, and infrastructure was tight, and now as its carefully laid systems and structures collapse, the country as a whole is crippled. It will take time to rebuild and reorganise, but if Mantetsu's influence was even greater, it could have been worse.
Post-Colonial Chaos
Mantetsu's grip on Fengtian's politics, economy and infrastructure was choking, and now as its carefully laid systems and structures collapse, the country as a whole is utterly crippled. It will take a very long time to rebuild and reorganise.
Disastrous Governance
The Recovery League's thorough grip on power has begun to fray the state's already tenuous grasp on legitimacy.
Army Dominance
The Zhang Clique and the Army have a thorough grip on government, causing the other political factions to turn to unconventional means to limit their control. Unfortunately, these means and the Zhang Clique's abuses of power have dire consequences.
Plutocratic Exploitation
The Communications Clique's iron grip on the nation's government has allowed it to engage in an entirely new level of exploitation and greed, reducing the state's legitimacy and attracting unprecedented Japanese political pressure.
The Heilongjiang Defection
Having long been a rival and opponent of Yang Yuting under the guise of the late Zhang Zuolin's tenure in the Three Northeastern Provinces, Ma Zhanshan and Zhang's close allies from his days as a bandit, the Heilongjiang Clique, have defected following Yuting's assumption as Grand Marshal of the Fengtian Government. Taking with them the equivalent of 3 million silver dollars from the reserve, it has had a sordid effect on the administration's financial capacity.
The Heilongjiang Insurgency
Denied their offering of service to the enemy, the Heilongjiang Clique of Ma Zhanshan, Wan Fulin, and Wu Junsheng have decided to take matters into their own hands. Staging a call for national resistance across radio channels in the Northeast, they have begun to sap potential recruits to their cause, and attack various garrisons all across Dongbei. Whilst unlikely to transform into a full-scale revolt against the new Fengtian authorities, it is nonetheless a pressing matter that requires considerable government attention, much of which could be directed towards the interior.
The Legations Deal
Through some clever politicking, and perhaps some backroom 'negotiation', the Economic Minister has secured a valuable trade deal with the Legation Cities.

Suppressed Labour Movement
Although labourers have become a crucial part of Chinese society, they have also become a hotbed for the burgeoning Chinese socialist movement. Such ideals have always been and shall continue to be the disease of the heart, and the Anguojun shall provide the necessary cure to such an ailment.
Worker Loyalty
If our nation shall one day achieve anything close to the power of the Great Dynasties of old, then our nation must be of one mind. Talk of class warfare only divides the people when national success brings prosperity to all walks of life. Just as the Grand Marshal must have the people's best interests at heart, so too must all classes have the nation's best interests at heart. Only then shall the Chinese people reap the rewards of faith, and surpass even the greatest empires of the West.
Centralised Provincial Revenues
During the Heights of the Warlord Era, any warlord could claim Beijing or Guangzhou on their own and concurrently become the President of the Republic. As such, the provinces zealously guarded their wealth from being taxed by rivals on the Republican throne, instead opting to utilise provincial revenues to fund their own armies and local economies.\n\nSuch a time of disunity has come to an end now, with the triumph of the Anguojun over its greatest rivals. If China is to become strong once more, then the entire nation must operate under a singular vision, just as a symphony must follow the whims of one sole conductor. Parallel tax codes and legal systems must be abolished, and all shall bend the knee to China's true government.
Primacy of the Loyalists
Unlike the pompous Wu Peifu who attended the great Baoding Academy and the liberal intellectuals of the south who scoff at the Fengtian Government, our Marshal Zhang came from nothing. He was born into abject poverty, and became a bandit in his youth. It was during this time that Zhang met many like him, and forged with them a brotherhood of steel. These bands of brothers were collectively absorbed into the Qing military following the Russo-Japanese War, and sided with the Imperial Government and Beiyang Army during the Xinhai Revolution.\n\nZhang and his brothers came to form the nucleus of the Fengtian Clique, and this tight-knit assortment of bandits-turned-warlords were able to achieve political dominance over China for a time. Even though Marshal Zhang's government ended up losing Beijing in 1927, the Fengtian Clique's cohesive structure allowed them to once again claim control over the Forbidden City. It was through friends and family that Marshal Zhang was able to achieve final victory over his rivals, and his allies will continue to serve as the core of the Anguojun military force.
Thorough Command Reforms
Every military clique in China has its centre, but it is not the centre that often leads to victory. No, it is the efforts and sacrifice of its most diligent, those who dare to dream of greatness and those who are not afraid to take it. While the Japanese military has adopted meritorious reforms, it seems that China and the Fengtian Clique continue to lag behind on such measures. The Grand Marshal must see to it that the Chinese military is not purely structured around his friends and family, but also the best and brightest young stars who emerge from the haystack, who shall continue to perform great deeds in service to the nation, and perhaps lead it one day.
Triumph of the Model Officers
In Japan, many promising young Chinese students learned how to conduct war in the Japanese fashion. Upon returning home, they brought their knowledge with them, and transformed the military around themselves. Sun Chuanfang rose to become not just a petty warlord, but master of Eastern China. Chiang Kai-shek became the military director of the Kuomintang, and was responsible for the training of Whampoa students. Meanwhile in the Fengtian Clique, the Shikan Clique has been responsible for many of Marshal Zhang's victories. The Marshal has recognised the achievements of the meritorious, and has allowed their methods to be the guiding force of the new Chinese military.

With the chaos and destruction of war, and its separation from food-rich areas to the south and west, the region's new occupiers are struggling to maintain order and keep their own troops fed.

Local Armoured Warfare Programme
The popular image of a warlord is that of an arbitrary tyrant: a cruel, uneducated autocrat with little regard to human life, ceaseless avarice, and surrounded by a decadent court of vice and yesmen. The reality is much more nuanced. Many warlords were well-educated and kept up to date with international political trends, and while most had a ruthless streak, that was hardly uncommon in China. Furthermore, while most were autocrats, they hardly ruled alone: they were backed by a complex web of politicians, generals, economic elites, social figures, and intellectuals.
Federalist Spirit: §cTwin Dragons Taming the Water§!
The modern Chinese Federalist rose and fell across the first half of the 1920s. A coalition of constitutionalists, democrats, and regionalists - they banded together amid the continued North-South stalemate at the peak of the warlord era. Their calls for the various provinces to work towards implementing local self-government and then peacefully unite together into a federal republic achieved some traction, but after a promising start it was rejected by both northern and southern governments, with further discrediting by the Zhili's successful unification by force.\n\nIn what almost seems like a cruel joke, it would appear that the final attempt to bridge the North-South divide as of recent has proved its most fruitful; finally, after decades, the nation is united in somewhat amiable terms. Albeit, the situation is far from genuine. With Zhang Junmai thrust into the position of compromise Premier for a President who would rather surf the delights of hedonism than heed governance, the government has found itself miraculously inefficient at even the most basic conducts of Governance. United on the surface, it takes but one glance beneath to witness all the cracks manifesting in the Republic's hastily composed structures.
Political Legitimacy: §cThe FInely Oiled Machine§!
$FNG_beiyang_popular_support_intro$\n\nRuling akin to how an entrepreneur runs a business, the various maestros, masters, and suits underneath the aloof President Xueliang have been emboldened once more to conduct statecraft as they deem fit. Deigned with assets, influence, knowledge and know-how, the Communication's Clique have risen far from their once lowly heights of shattered irrelevancy into that of national prominence. Anyone who is anyone, or wants to be, must grease the wheels of Communication's political machine, and in return be rewarded handsomely for their efforts. Politics and the meddling of politicians may take the backseat, for economic management and reconstruction are the necessary antidotes for China's woes.
Political Legitimacy: §gIn the Eye of the Beiyang Tiger§!
$FNG_beiyang_popular_support_intro$\n\nMiraculously, it would appear that the lessons learned by Duan Qirui and his Anhui Clique did not necessarily die with their loss of status; for their methods have been observed, studied, and reinforced into an entirely new-method of dominant rulership. Once a motley crew of exiled politicians and failures, the Recovery League has managed to bolster its numbers with undeniable expertise under the guise of the Five Races, and through the efforts of men such as Pan Fu, Gu Weijun, and Wang Yitang, the Old Marshal appears to have had his wish granted; a state utterly subservient to him and his family, staffed by wise scholars akin to the days of old.
Political Legitimacy: §nStewardship of Providence§!

In a Napoleonic demeanour, in conjunction with the lessons learned from the Japanese, and collaborating with the Communication's Clique and Young China Party, President Yang has restored modernity, progress, and vitality to the ailing Middle Kingdom.

Political Legitimacy: §gBeiyang's Compradors§!
$FNG_beiyang_popular_support_intro$\n\nDeveloping a knack for political survival in the least likely of circumstances, President Wang Yitang and the various members of the Recovery League, once Marshal Zhang's common courtiers, have managed to rally the forces of the Five Races Under One Union into a new Beiyang Republic, auspciously under Japanese watch. Without having bend to the whims of of autocrats or superiors, bar Tokyo, Wang has been granted the full capacities of his position to implement his desired social policies reminiscent of his time during the heyday of the Anfu Club. Whatever the case may be, Wang's policies serve to benefit the Japanese first, and his people second, even if he is unwilling.
Political Legitimacy: §cGovernance of Monopolies§!
$FNG_beiyang_popular_support_intro$\n\nOnce scuttered to political irrelevancy following the November Riots, the New Communications Clique's term in the shadows would see a brief resurgence of its old rivals in the Old Communications Clique; Liang Shiyi and Zhou Ziqi. Ultimately however, with the reliance of the Fengtian Clique on Japan and the resurgence of Pro-Japanese policy, men once considered traitos such as Zhang Zongxiang, Lu Zongyu and Cao Rulin were able to claw back their relevancy. Furthermore ascending under the Japanese instituted government, the New Communications Clique seeks to finalise its mission of the 1910s: to industrialise and modernise the nation, and rake in the profits whilst doing so.
Waging the War of Minds and Bodies
The Reformed Government of China stands as a beacon of law and order, starkly against the chaos that has engulfed China ever since the National Protection War. However, the government must continue to consolidate control of the hinterlands, as rebels continue to agitate against the new order in Asia. The people will eventually lose respect for our government too, should these insurrectionists continue to mount insult after insult to the [ROOT.GetLeader] administration. The Reformed Government must root out these parasites and deal with them accordingly.
War of National Pacification
Although Japan and China continue to stand as the two pillars of Asian ascendancy, the Dragon cannot continue to solely eat from the hands of the Rising Sun. The New China must organise an army strong enough to consolidate China by itself, against all agitators who seek to plunge our nation back into its darkest hour. The Heping Jianguojun stands strong, the Heping Jianguojun stands firm. Zhonghua Minguo wansui!

Reviving Chinese Financial Stability
Suffice to say, China's financial situation has been less than ideal. With the majority of its banking wealth absorbed into coastal cities such as Tianjin, Hong Kong, or Shanghai, the stability of the nation's finance lies much outside its own control. Similarly, decades of warfare and the lack of a true, strong, resilient Central Government has resulted both in a distrust for Chinese credit, an influx in inordinate local currencies, and even the hoarding of assets in times of great struggle. It will take a monumental effort, but the government can at least work towards rebuilding China's commerce.
Pacification by Chinese Might
Like in the days of the Jin Dynasty, President Yuan Shikai was unable to maintain order across the Middle Kingdom and the Central State once again plunged into chaos, as two governments emerged, each claiming to represent all of China. Marshal [ROOT.GetLeader]'s government inherits the legacy of the Beiyang Army, the most righteous and modernising force across all China.\n\nMeanwhile, the ignoble Guangzhou Government claims succession from the vile Sun Yat-sen who in his derangement brought the scourge of Marxism into our sacred nation's heart. Against liberals who foolishly call themselves humane and socialist bandits who steal from rich and poor alike, the Anguojun Government marches forward to restore not just order, but spiritual restoration to a nation suffering from the sickness of imperialism.
Maximising Production Line Efficiency
In the West, superior manufacturing has resulted in the shifting of borders and the toppling of Empires. While Fengtian boasts the greatest industrial base in all of China, such industrial might is useless if it isn't harnessed to its fullest potential. The Empire of Japan to the East and the Russian Bear to the North wield far superior manufacturing methods to our own, and if China is to freed by itself, then the Anguojun Government must institute much-needed production regulations and organisation in order to produce enough military equipment to ensure the Anguojun remains the best supplied force in the nation.
Intolerable Political Realities
Although the Fengtian Government stands once more as the true Central Government based in Beijing, a Government of Tradition and Order seems to continue to elude the Chinese people. The Anguojun continue to support such lofty ideals, but the provisional government, which previously only ruled in Shenyang, is currently unsuitable to administer provinces south of the Great Wall with great effectiveness. Governance barely extends beyond city walls, and many administrative posts remain vacant as [ROOT.GetLeader]'s administration scrambles to fill in all the posts.
Endemic Economic Malaise
In 1926, Zhang Zuolin found the Fengtian Dollar struggling to maintain value and hoped to secure foreign loans to sustain the ailing economy. The Northern Expedition only served to exacerbate the fragile economy, and the Fengtian Dollar suffered collapse after Wu's Zhili Clique pushed Zhang back across the Great Wall. Such was the state of the Northeastern economy that the Russian opportunists attempted to encroach on Chinese land, which was only stopped by capitulation to the Japanese.\n\nAlthough Japanese aid largely restabilised Anguojun finances, it would seem that the National Reclamation War has once again rendered the Fengtian economy on the brink. Many foreign businesses find themselves unwilling to operate in our lands so long as banditry and violence remains prevalent in urban centres, and many Chinese businesses which operated based on the Zhili order have now found themselves displaced in the New China. Marshal [ROOT.GetLeader] must see the economic woes patched or risk losing the support of the people.
Crippling Army Rivalries
Although the Fengtian Clique remains one of the more cohesive military cliques operating in China, it too has also been prone to division. While Marshal Zhang Zuolin and his sworn-brothers formed the nucleus of the army initially, the Fengtian Army developed its own assortment of Young Guard factions in the coming years. Zhang's oldest son Zhang Xueliang upon graduating from the Fengtian Military Academy established his own inner circle within the Fengtian Military, which came to be known as the Shaoshuai Clique. When Zhang welcomed Yang Yuting and other Japanese-trained NCOs into the Fengtian military, these officers formed the Shikan Clique, which called for Japanese-inspired military reforms.\n\nA third progressive Young Guard faction was established by the rising Fengtian officer Guo Songling, who utterly despised Yang and his Shikan Clique. Ultimately, Guo would lead a rebellion following the 2nd Zhifeng War which resulted in his death and the destruction of his posse, but the scars of the Anti-Fengtian revolt continue to reverberate in the Anguojun Army. Zhang Xueliang never forgave Yang's execution of his old friend and mentor, and this second Fengtian victory has once again led to increased ambitions and heightened tensions. Should [ROOT.GetLeader] hope to maintain an orderly regime, he must see to it that a Anti-Fengtian revolt does not occur under his watch.
An Army of Traitors
What duty or honour is there to derive from an institution deployed against its own countrymen? Such is a question that looms large and with longevitiy in the minds of many of the Heping Jianguojun's common soldiers. Money is an incentive, of course, but it cannot cleanse one's own soul. Those few men of military talent that opted for collaboration remain sparce and scattered, whilst the army itself is incredibly reliant upon Japanese arms and materiel to support even the most basic of garrison efforts.

Collaboration: The Great Evil
Hanjian. That is the term they use to describe those within the current government. Traitors not only to their country, but to the whole Chinese race. But collaboration is a complex construct, and the various individuals gathered under the halls of the new Chinese administration have all reached the embrace of Tokyo for various reasons. Numbering among them: genuine sympathy, material conditions, dissonance with the previous power structures, and so on. Yet not all collaborators are equal, especially those unwilling or otherwise forced. Nonetheless, the sin they have committed is great, and the nation will not soon forget it.
The New Oligarchy
In the Imperial Era, society was led by the prosperous gentry class, and learned scholarly men. Such men will continue to hold high status in the New China, but the realities of our nation demand a new elite to lead the charge forward. In the West, it was the plutocratic class and industrious businessmen who brought about economic modernisation, and the Chinese people must learn from their successes whilst avoiding their mistakes. Yesterday's China was the Great Empire of the Past, Today's China is the sleeping tiger, and Tomorrow's China is the Dragon Reborn.
Achieving National Statism
Zeng Qi and his friends learned much from their squabbles with their old Marxist friends. While they fell into the delusion of international socialism, Zeng understood that socialism is best implemented for the cause of the home nation alone. Coining such an ideology as National Statism, it became the pillar of the Young China Party. China will be reborn not through the death of the Old China, but a celebration of both Old and New China to truly honour the dream of 1911, and establish a Nationalistic, Corporatist, and Confucian China.
True Equality of the Five Races
Unlike the Southern rebels who fought for a Han China, the New China built from the experiences of the Northeast fights for all races under its flag. The Concordia Association was founded to bring about ethnic harmony across Dongbei, and now such dreams will flower not only in Heilongjiang, but in the far reaches of the nation, from Kunming to Hulunbuir, from Kashgar to Harbin! Together, the equal races shall build a fairer China, one that shall usher in a new era of peace and prosperity.
Financing Reformed Reconstruction
Deft diplomats and experts at business management, the New Communications Clique have managed to secure lucrative loans, fantastic trade deals, and the compliance of other industrial and merchant groups within China in order to finacne their grand plans for national economic reconstruction. Whilst observers would decry the establishment of monopolies and massive conglomerates of businesses, the necessary endeavours required by the state to pursue national revival cannot be produced merely by petty capital.

Anshan Iron & Steel has been a Sino-Japanese joint company ever since its establishment in 1916, with both sides having a measure of control over its management, profits, and product. Now Mantetsu wants to buy the company, and officially rename it 'Shōwa Steel'. Supposedly under their management the operation will be more efficient, and a measure of the profits and product will still make their way to our coffers.
Revise our Position on Looting
Our decision to permit looting of occupied areas may have been a mistake. Unfortunately rescinding popular orders after they've been given, not to mention restraining the men, will not be an easy undertaking.
Prevent looting in Zhili
It is said that the people fear soldiers like a flood, or like vicious beasts - they flee for their lives in terror.
Prevent looting in Henan
It is said that the people fear soldiers like a flood, or like vicious beasts - they flee for their lives in terror.
Prevent looting in Wuhan
It is said that the people fear soldiers like a flood, or like vicious beasts - they flee for their lives in terror. We must bring a halt to the chaos in Wuhan, or else see our national legitimacy suffer.
The Soy Agricultural Initiative
Fengtian's significant Korean minority are skilled rice planters, but soybeans have become an extremely desirable cash crop, as they provide not only an excellent source of food, fertiliser, and animal feed, but also an oil with industrial applications. Mantetsu undertook an effort to educate Koreans in Soy farming, but the response has been mixed. They now want our help to push this through.
Study Japanese Manufacturing Methods
Japan has fielded an industrial sector resembling those in the West for decades, far outstripping anything in Manchuria. We must learn all they will let us, and more.
Request Japanese Infantry Equipment
Japan has long provided us with a variety of military equipment, surely it can't hurt to ask for more.
Request Japanese Artillery
Japan's Kokura Arsenal has a long history of producing quality artillery, which would be of great assistance to our efforts.
Request Japanese Tanks
Japanese industry can produce tanks in enormous quantities far exceeding our own. Surely they must have some to spare.
Preparing for the Prince's Visit
The Japanese Emperor's uncle, Prince Kan'in Kotohito, will be arriving to tour the Northeast later this year. For such an honoured guest, especially one who could greatly shape the Shenyang-Tokyo relationship, we must ensure that everything is made eminently presentable. Rumours of a nationalist plot against the Prince's life must also be put to rest.
Increase Security in Shenyang
As rumours of a plot against the Japanese Prince's life swirl, we must improve security in the capital. While the rest of his visit may be unpredictable, it is no secret that he will visit both the Government and the Grand Marshal in Shenyang.
Investigate the Junior Officer Corps
While many idealistic younger officers openly agitate against the regressive Zhili regime to the south, as is appropriate, others also see Japan as an enemy. While their views may have some merit, we cannot allow these hot-headed individuals to sabotage the important Shenyang-Tokyo relationship.
Reinforce Soldierly Discipline
We cannot afford to have slovenly soldiers on display when Prince Kan'in Kotohito visits the troops. Nor can we permit dangerous radicals to be present.
Present Chinese Modernity
China is not a modern country, but with our recent efforts and a fresh coat of paint it might appear to be.
Militarise the Minsheng Truck
In the early 1930s Zhang Xueliang commissioned an American engineer to create China's first domestically produced automobile called 'Minsheng' or 'people's livelihood'. While never mass-produced, with the right modifications these hardy trucks could be adapted to serve military purposes.
Create Fortress Manchuria
The Yan Mountains to the South, the Lesser Khigan Range to the West, and the Bohai Gulf to the East create a natural fortress around the Manchurian plain, leaving the Shanhai Pass as the only easy point of entry. It is easy to fortify the Northeast when nature has already done so much of the work.
Rebuild the Second Army
The Fengtian Second Army, often called the 'Zhili Army' due to its recruiting grounds in Zhili Province, was one of Zhang Zuolin's premier fighting forces during the Zhifeng Wars. The unit suffered a loss of leadership following the defection of Guo Songling in 1925, and in 1928 its beleaguered soldiers found themselves stranded in Shandong. The subsequent peace saw this prestigious unit gradually disintegrate, as veterans enlisted with Zhang Zongchang, left for Manchuria, or returned to their families in Zhili. With North China again in our grasp, the time has come to raise the Second Army's old banner and return its name to glory!
Raise Independent Brigades in Dezhou
The collapse of [QIE.GetNameDef] has left broad swathes of the North China Plain open to marauding bandits, both those native to the region and former [QIE.GetName] troops turned criminal. With our lax policies on looting, it shouldn't be hard to rally these men and reorganise them into 'independent brigades'.
Raise Independent Brigades in Kaifeng
The collapse of [QIE.GetNameDef] has left broad swathes of the North China Plain open to marauding bandits, both those native to the region and former [QIE.GetName] troops turned criminal. With our lax policies on looting, it shouldn't be hard to rally these men and reorganise them into 'independent brigades'.
Raise Independent Brigades in Ruyang
The collapse of [QIE.GetNameDef] has left broad swathes of the North China Plain open to marauding bandits, both those native to the region and former [QIE.GetName] troops turned criminal. With our lax policies on looting, it shouldn't be hard to rally these men and reorganise them into 'independent brigades'.
Raise Independent Brigades in Guanzhong
The collapse of [QIE.GetNameDef] has left broad swathes of the North China Plain open to marauding bandits, both those native to the region and former [QIE.GetName] troops turned criminal. With our lax policies on looting, it shouldn't be hard to rally these men and reorganise them into 'independent brigades'.
Raise the Baoding Cadet Corps
The young Baoding Cadets were among the most vocal supporters of the Manchu monarchy in Beijing, and our victory in north China left all but a few imprisoned or sent home. Now the time has come for these men to fight on the right side of history. While some may question arming former enemies, their patriotism is unquestionable and in such dire times the country must come first.
Centralise the Banks
Fengtian currently features four note-issuing banks, namely the Bank of the Three Eastern Provinces, the Bank of Jilin, the Bank of Heilongjiang and the Frontier Bank, each of which are products of earlier centralisation efforts. Now it seems pertinent to complete this process and unify them all under a single Central Bank.
Re-Introduce the Fengtian Dollar
The Fengtian Dollar was one of former Civil Governor Wang Yongjiang's later experiments, and served as a currency not backed by silver but still payable in tax, demonstrating the government's faith in its value but requiring no extra silver to print. Following enormous government expenditures during the last Zhifeng War and subsequent inflation, the currency was discontinued, but its flexibility could be useful today in attracting additional investment.
Fill the Silver Reserve
The Fengtian Yuan, our principal currency, is backed by silver and in the past has even gained value against the Japanese Yen. This has been met by Japanese insistence that our reserves have never held enough silver to properly back the currency. Regrettably there may have been some truth to this, and so more silver must be purchased if we are to attract additional investment.
Solicit Chinese Investment
Chinese investment is at the heart of our efforts to return at least some control of Fengtian's economy to its people, instead of foreign powers. Incentives and careful planning are the only way forward.
Encourage Domestic Materials Investment
Worried by Japanese dominance of Fengtian's heavy industry sector, several wealthy businessmen with ties to the Communications Clique have offered to pool their resources to invest in several promising companies in Jinzhou, namely Zhaozin Ceramics Company, Jinzhou Railway Machinery, and the Northeastern Chemical Leather Plant.
Approve Domestic Investment in Heilongjiang
With Japanese investment often flooding into heavy industry and mining, a group of local investors have decided to pool their resources in order to back two Chinese companies struggling against Mantetsu competition. The Dongdai Fertiliser company and Shanjing Packing Plant will both continue to help Fengtian's burgeoning soy industry expand into the Northeastern frontier.
Solicit Japanese Investment
Unfortunately foreign capital is crucial to our development efforts, and so we must make attempts to attract Japanese alongside Chinese investors. While they won't receive the same incentives as our own citizens, they should be comforted by our recent filling of the silver reserves.
Mitsui Investment in Light Industry
Representatives of the Mitsui Zaibatsu are hoping to invest heavily in local businesses, specifically Dongxing Dye & Textile Company, Fengtian Industrial Paper, and Dongbei Glass. With controlling shares in all three companies, Mitsui would likely dominate our glass, paper, and textile industries for the foreseeable future, with only Mantetsu as competition.
Japanese Investment in Shipping and Tourism
Mantetsu has actively promoted tourism in China for years, drawing wealthy and middle class tourists to ride across Manchuria's 'exotic landscape' on its state of the art railways. However, its ambitions have never extended to the sea.\n\nA small group of wealthy investors from Tokyo now hope to partner with several local shipping companies and establish a water-borne alternative to Mantetsu's railway tourism, while performing shipping services on the side, thus creating 'Bohai Waterborne Enterprises'.\n
Sumitomo Minerals and Metals Investment
After talks with government representatives, the Sumitomo Zaibatsu has agreed to partially fund metals and mineral prospecting across Fengtian, in return for a proportional share in any companies created to extract any resources discovered. With rumours of gold in the Khigan Mountains and Tungsten in Fengtian province, their investment seems likely to pan out.
Approve Further Expansion at Anshan
With recent government funded expansion of the Anshan Mines and an atmosphere ripe for investment, Mantetsu has hopes to invest further capital in modernising and expanding its operations in and around Anshan.
Solicit Russian Investors
With the souring of relations with the Japanese, we no longer have access to our main source of foreign capital. While relations with the Russians recently have not been the best, we may be able to entice certain powerful Siberian businessmen to invest in our provinces along the border.
Upgrade Harbin Port Facilities
Since its construction at the end of the 19th century, Harbin's port has been an important economic asset to the area surrounding it, allowing goods to be shipped along the Songhua and Amur rivers. With the departure of the Japanese, Dalzavod is willing to invest in expanding Harbin's port facilities, resulting in increased trade between Northeastern China and the Russian Far East.
Heilongjiang Minerals Investment
With rumours of gold being discovered in northern Heilongjiang, the Amur Gold Mining Society is seemingly willing to invest in gold mining and prospecting operations along the Russian border. While they would get a significant portion of any resources extracted, it may prove useful in developing remote communities and provide our government with much needed wealth, as well as expanding general resource extraction capabilities in those regions.
Railway Construction
The Northeast has more railways than any other region of China, but virtually all of those of strategic relevance are owned and maintained by Mantetsu, on behalf of the Japanese Government. The National Transportation Commission wants to expand the smaller Chinese-owned network to in part to improve our infrastructure, but more importantly to reduce our strategic reliance on the Japanese.
Develop Infrastructure in Liaoning
Develop Infrastructure in Liaobei and Jilin
Develop Infrastructure in Nenjinang and Songjiang
Finish the Jilin-Shenyang Line
The reorganised NTC's first major project is finishing the Jilin-Shenyang Railway. Originally it was planned in 1927 by Zhang Zuoxiang as a way to counteract Japanese influence in his province. Unfortunately, the project met serious delays due to the eruption of war in the south, and Japanese attempts to stall construction. The line has been operating in limited capacity since 1931, but remains incapable of fulfilling its true purpose; providing a Chinese-controlled strategic alternative to the main line of the South Manchuria Railway. As an added bonus, it would bring additional economic development to areas of Jilin province not connected to the South Manchuria Railway's main line.
Finish the Pingqi Line
The NTC's next major project is the Siping-Qiqihar Line, or Pingqi line, which was originally proposed by the Japanese as part of a larger project to connect Mantetsu's smaller provincial lines with central lines running through major cities. Nearing completion in late 1927, any further construction was halted due to turmoil in the south and the need for funds elsewhere. While Mantetsu still holds significant control over the line at the moment, finishing the line should give us the edge needed to control it. However, most significantly, its completion would allow us to bypass the South Manchuria Railway when moving troops north towards Heilongjiang, thus decreasing Japan's control over our strategic decisions. Furthermore, an upgrade to the Pingqi line should also bring some much needed economic development to the relatively undeveloped northern reaches of Fengtian province.
Upgrade the Shenyang-Chengde Line
With the NTC's recent railway building spree providing more strategic flexibility when it comes to troop and resource movement within the northeast, it can finally turn its attention to our end goal, the reclamation of Beijing. With the opening of the Jincheng line as an extension of the pre-existing Shenyang-Shanhaiguan railway in 1934, Rehe was connected to the rest of the northeastern railway system thus allowing for greater logistical capabilities in the area. Upgrading this line should allow for our forces near the great wall to be better supplied when the inevitable conflict with our southern enemies finally occurs.

Japanese Patience Runs Thin
The Imperial Court, at behest of the Tianjin Army, has begrudgingly offered their support for our War of National Reclamation. But we are on a short leash - the Kwantung Army and others fear the possibility of losing control of Manchuria and doubt our ability to achieve definitive results. Should we fail to take key objectives, most notably Beijing, in time or worse should we be driven back - the Kwantung Army may seize the moment to install one of the puppets into power.
Buy Time with the Emperor
Zhang has always been careful about his relationship with Japan, never wanting to appear submissive to avoid offending Chinese nationalists but also maintaining a friendly appearance to ensure the steady flow of Japanese aid. It is well known by now that the Imperial Court does not have total control over its armies, but that does not mean we can ignore them either. Pleading our case with Japanese Officials, with the Tianjin Army faction as our intermediaries, will help keep a lid on Japanese pressure.
Crack Down on Sedition
Various Japanese agents have sought to penetrate major organs in our government, bribing and corrupting our officials and commanders. They have sought to expand Japanese influence in civilian affairs, pulling figures from the various Fengtian Clique factions into their sphere. All of this has undermined Zhang's control over his own government, and making an example out of a few ringleaders will send a proper message about loyalty across Dongbei.
Curtail the Shikan Clique
In the military realm, Japanese Advisors have courted various officers up and down the command hierarchy to promote their influence with the army. The Shikan Clique in particular have been favourites of the Kwantung Army, many of them cultivated during their early military studies in Japan. Reassigning them from prominent positions, purging any open malcontents, and breaking up their networks will minimise their influence even if it disrupts the war effort and validates their beliefs that this war is debilitating.
Concessions to Concordia
The Concordia Association is the civilian front of Japanese imperialism, a group of bureaucrats, businessmen, and politicians ostensibly standing for promoting Pan-Asianism and Sino-Japanese trade ties. An extension of Japanese control over our railways, they have branched quickly into mining and government. Though ultimately a threat to our independence, we may need to work with them to check their more radical Kwantung Army peers.

Rein in the Extremists

Deploy Emergency Economic Aid
Though Manchuria was once the most industrialised part of China, economic malaise and a determined effort to catch up by the Zhili has closed the gap. The Fengtian Government is struggling heavily to maintain its war footing and with our interests so heavily intertwined with their economy, it is up to us to provide an emergency injection of financial aid to prop up their war effort. We shall funnel money, technical experts, and machines through the Concordia Association, and with any luck they will survive long enough to repay us for what they owe.
Send Emergency Arms Shipment
Supplying a force capable of fighting a major war such as the Fengtian Army is no easy task and it is rapidly outstripping their military industrial base's capacity to do so. Our planners have proposed sending a massive shipment of rifles, artillery, and other supplies to keep the Fengtian Army in the field (especially units sympathetic to us), and hopefully keep the tide of the war in our favour.

Radicals
Independent Radicals and Revolutionaries\n§LThe revolutionary strain of radicalism within China has a fascinating history emanating from the timeless struggle of martyrs and heroes in the struggle against perceived injustices. Mobilising the fury of the masses, various revolutionaries have come and went, either peacefully or through fire and war. Largely coalescing into various parties such as the Kuomintang, or Young China Party, the revolutionary strain of thought is largely in contention with that of the reformists.\n\nThe allure of radicalism extends all across China however, from the steppe of the Northwest Frontier to the bustling streets of Shanghai, many cling to the ideals of a radically transformed China, either in the socialist egalitarian ideal, or in the strong nationalist flavour. Operating either under the radical elements of the Kuomintang, Young China Party, or Chinese Syndicalist party, the extremist groups refuse to partake in the Chinese Parliamentary system; seeing the newly proclaimed Central Government as merely a betrayal of the socialist revolution.§!\n
CSP
Chinese Syndicalist Party (Zhongguo Gongtuandang)\n§LLargely confined to urban centres or port cities, the Chinese Syndicalist Party for years remained merely a fragmented junior party of the Chinese Kuomintang. Considered to be milquetoast radicals espousing a foreign ideology in a nation without the large worker support base akin to that in Europe or the Americas, the Chinese Syndicalist Party still maintained significant successes in its political history. With key action in historical events such as the Hong Kong-Canton strikes in 1925, which resulted in the founding of the League of Chinese Syndicalists, or the Shanghai Uprising in 1932 which resulted in broad national mass action.\n\nWith its inherently pluralistic nature, the Chinese Syndicalist Party has found itself fragmented with a series of disparate cliques. Within the Northeast however, they are largely confined to a band of guerrillas led by Guan Xiangying, a stark divergence from their interior reliance on the urban working population; albeit they are little more than a political boogeyman.§!\n
KMT
Chinese Kuomintang (Zhongguo Guomindang)\n§LThe Chinese Nationalist Party has taken on many forms in its marred history. Founded as the parliamentary organisation of the Tongmenghui in 1912 by Sun Yat-sen, Huang Xing, and Song Jiaoren, the Kuomintang would endeavour itself to faithfully serve as a parliamentary party within the early Beiyang Republic. After Song's assassination and Sun's subsequent multiple exiles however, the Party would be reorganised into the Chinese Gemingang, and later revived as the Guomindang on October 10th 1919. Dedicated to the Three Principles of the People as espoused by Dr. Sun Yat-sen, the Kuomintang aspires for the implementation of the Party-State, or Dangguo, and implement the Three-Stage National Revolution. Through the aspiration for the Three Principles of Minzu, Minquan, and Minsheng (Nationalism, Democracy, and Welfare respectively), they hope to see a new revolutionary republic.\n\nDriven underground in 1927, their limited influence within pockets of revolutionary utopias and fluffy exiles scant make any difference within the Northeast, with the largest cell of sympathisers known as the Northeast Anti-Japanese National Salvation Directorate under Reorganisation Comrades Association cadre Zhu Jiqing.§!\n
NPSHA
Northeast People's Self-Help Association (Dongbei minzhong zijiu hui)\n§LFormed from the brief liberalisation period of the late 1920s and early 1930s, the United National Construction League would ultimately be banned, but as a result opened the doors to the formation of the Federation of Chinese Democratic Parties. A national movement spanning from North to South, the FCDP sought to unite all those parties seeking Constitutionalism and Liberal Democracy under one banner. With their efforts, they would champion the cause of true freedom for the Chinese people, and inevitably force even the mightiest warlord to bow to the fury of intellectuals and the masses.\n\nWhilst the Constitutionalists, and especially Zhang Junmai's National Renaissance Society, are persona non grata across the Great Wall, various members of Zhang Junmai's clique have setup shop within the Northeast, generally surrounding around Zhou Jngwen. In 1933 he organised the Northeast People's Self-Help Association as an extension of the Leftist strain of the Chinese Constitutionalist Party, in response to the 1932 Shanghai Uprising, acting as an orbiting faction within the CCP.§!\n
Republicans
Independent Republicans\n§LThe Beiyang government included many political independents, a tradition upheld in the Fengtian assembly. While perhaps united in a common desire for a constitutionalist, civilian ruled future, their unwillingness (or inability) to organise at a higher level has limited their options. Indeed, for a given issue they rarely vote as a united bloc, with legislators either swayed or bribed or threatened into a side.\n\nNevertheless, they are still a potent establishment force and provide hope for a constitutionalist, civilian ruled future. Their dreams of democratic reforms however are bound to be tempered by the realities they find themselves in. Few dare to speak out, though those that do clearly dream of a much more democratic republic.§!\n
Restoration Society
Restoration Society (Guangfuhui)\n§LOriginally founded in 1904 as the Military National Education Association by Tao Chengzhang, Zhang Taiyan, Cai Yuanpei, Gong Baoquan and Wei Lan, the future Restoraion Society was a Shanghai based revolutionary organisation that spanned into Jiangsu and Zhejiang. Fiercely anti-Manchu, the Restoration Society used various institutions such as Xu Xilin's Datong School to create a paramilitary bloc of revolutionary cadres ready to \
Communications Clique
Communications Clique (Jiaotongxi)\n§LThe sole politically coherent faction to emerge from the former Beiyang Government, the Communications Clique was founded on the cusp of the Xinhai Revolution by Tang Shaoyi, albeit it is most largely associated with the likes of Liang Shiyi, its long-term leader and one of its most high profile members. Centred around the Ministry of Posts and Communications, responsible for railways, postal services, shipping, telephones, and the Bank of Communications, the Communications Clique was crucial in the old Beiyang Government for its immense amount of wealth and revenues.\n\nStrongly supporting Yuan Shikai's restoration of the monarchy, somewhat out of conviction and somewhat out of self-servitude, the \
Recovery League
Recovery League (Guangfuxi)\n§LA loose association of fallen generals, governors, bureaucrats, and politicians without any strong ideological affiliation, most of whom find themselves in Fengtian because there are few other places where they might hold any semblance of power. Easily bribed and tempted, they often serve to promote the interests of whoever is willing to pay, and consequently the \
Zhang Clique
Zhang Clique (Zhanghui)\n§LRooted in the foundations of Zhang Zuolin's early career as a bandit and soldier, the Zhang Clique is but the largest overarching composite collection of various smaller organisations and factions, staffed by loyalists and generals. Whilst ideology is present within the statesmanship decisions of those within the Zhang Clique, it is secondary to loyalty towards Zhang Zuolin. Hardly capable of continuing to rule as mere military strongmen, the Zhang Clique's pretences to democracy and lack of general commitment to true ideology leaves it open and malleable to many interpretations of Chinese republicanism.\n\nWith smaller regional cliques all-throughout Dongbei, they function as interest groups within Zhang Zuolin's inner circle; the Heilongjiang Clique of Wan Fulin, Wu Junsheng, and Ma Zhanshan, or the Shaoshuai Clique of Zhang Xueliang, the Shikan Clique of Yang Yuting, or Jilin Clique of Zhang Zuoxiang, to name a few. Considered to have the greatest sway on Zuolin's political outlook, the Zhang Clique itself is ripe with infighting and squabbling as ideological convictions and loyalties mature, and wane.§!\n

Mantetsu Collaboration

The Fengtian Government Paraded Alone

Preservation of the Xinhai Revolution
Ironically, Fengtian is the sole national government upholding the order established by the Xinhai Revolution in 1911, which called for the overthrow of the Qing and the establishment of a Republic. Although its republican commitments are questionable, and Southern reclamation is currently unrealistic, the government has loudly advocated both goals, as they foster domestic legitimacy.
Fuguo Qiangbing
Translating roughly to 'Enrich the Country, Strengthen the Army', this proverb dates back to ancient legalist philosophers, but has been used more recently to inspire reforms in both Guangxu Era China and Meiji Era Japan. Now it is applied again in Fengtian, as the government seeks to modernise and eventually strike South against the resurgent Zhili Clique, and from there establish control over all China.
Open the Propaganda Front
Sometimes the most decisive battles are fought and won in hearts and minds. We have fought a passive war of words with [QIE.GetNameDef] ever since 1928, and now the time has come to begin a new offensive and redouble our efforts. Ten thousand years to the Republic!
Suppress Regionalist Sentiment
For many years, Zhang Zuolin's primary political slogan was 'The Northeast for the Northeast', but when his ambitions turned toward Beijing, this regionalist message had to be set aside. Ever since, it has proven a thorn in the Grand Marshal's side, and many still espouse these old sentiments. The time has come to put the matter to rest once and for all.
Silence Targeted Subversives
The regionalist movement has never been organised, but it has received support from the local gentry, school teachers, and government bureaucrats. Some of these figures have become increasingly prominent, and by silencing them we may cut the head from the regionalist snake. Some can be bribed, and others can be threatened or fired - to say nothing of other persuasive methods.
Justify Mass Arrests
So long as the regionalist movement remains peaceful, we lack the institutional and public support to crush it decisively. By dispatching agents disguised as protestors we can push the movement toward violent means, cost them their public support, and then justify mass arrests.
[FNG_Mantetsu_Collaboration_focus_name]
Mantetsu Collaboration
Seize Mantetsu Assets
[FNG_Mantetsu_Collaboration_focus_desc]
Mantetsu, also known as the 'South Manchuria Railway Company', exerts an enormous amount of control over our economy, with numerous subsidiaries ranging from flour mills to hospitals. Its aid will unfortunately be essential to developing most aspects of our economy that require Japanese technical expertise.
Before the Japanese withdrawal, Mantetsu was one of the most influential 'private' entities in all of Dongbei, possessing a wide variety of subsidiaries and assets ranging from railways to hospitals. Now that relations have soured with Japan, seizing Mantetsu's assets should allow us to regain control of and develop our economy.
[FNG_Yamato_Hotel_Licenses_focus_name]
Yamato Hotel Licences
Repurpose Yamato Hotel Franchises
[FNG_Yamato_Hotel_Licenses_focus_desc]
One of Mantetsu's most successful ventures in Manchuria is its Yamato Hotel franchise, which serves the countless Japanese businessmen who make their way to and from the Home Islands every day. Despite the unwelcome influence they bear, their skills and capital are crucial. We must decide their future.
With the departure of the Japanese, we have inherited several empty luxury hotels that won't be seeing any guests soon. Seeing as Japanese businessmen and dignitaries are unlikely to be visiting our territory any time soon, it would be helpful to convert these luxury hotels into something more useful.
Japanese Electrical Expertise
Thanks to China's backwardness over the past century, and the chaos of the past two decades, the country has few native engineers. Japanese assistance will be essential in bringing modernity to the Northeast.
[FNG_Mantetsu_Research_Wing_focus_name]
Mantetsu Research Wing
Expand Northeastern University
[FNG_Mantetsu_Research_Wing_focus_desc]
Mantetsu's Research Wing, known as 'Mantetsu Chōsabu', serves as the centrepiece of Japan's colonial programme, and pursues a wide variety of scientific goals. Its massive funding and talent pool could be of great use to us in our own efforts.
Established in 1902 as Fengtian University by Zhao Erxun, the then Viceroy of the Three Northeastern Provinces, Northeastern University would eventually become indispensable to the Northeast, being our main source of technical knowledge. Since we can no longer rely on the Japanese for technical assistance, it is imperative that we expand on our ability to develop technical expertise domestically.
Mantetsu Civil Engineering Projects
While the Japanese have much to benefit directly from large civil engineering projects in Fengtian, they also do so indirectly by helping to present our regime as successful at improving the everyday lives of citizens. In this respect, our interests are mutually aligned.
Develop the Northern Frontier
The northern reaches of Heilongjiang and Xing'an have been dominated by mountainous boreal forests since time immemorial, swept by bitter Siberian winds and inhabited only by passing nomads. Modern technologies could allow settlers to penetrate this hostile environment and pursue rumours of coal, gold, and graphite in the Khingan Mountains.
Fengtian Society for Light Metals
Significant deposits of Bauxite and Alunite have been known to exist in Fengtian province for many years, but recent advances by Mantetsu sponsored laboratories in Fushun and Tokyo have enabled Aluminium production via a number of electro-chemical processes.
Yalu and Songhua Hydroelectricity
Manchuria's abundant coal deposits make for an excellent power source, but the strong currents of the Yalu and Songhua rivers could provide additional power at minimal expense. With Japanese expertise, we might harness these mighty rivers to power more homes and industry.
Japanese Coal Gasification Methods
Japan's quest for crucial oil lead it to Manchuria, but now with disappointing results from prospecting, coal gasification seems the only logical path forward. Though energy intensive, Fushun's enormous coal deposits could make the complex processes worthwhile.
Manchurian Model Cities
Japan sometimes goes to surprising lengths to portray its role in Fengtian as one of benevolent paternalism, to which end Mantetsu plans to install state of the art electrical, sewer, and tram systems in the major cities of Shenyang, Changchun, and Harbin.
Found the Northeast IDC
At Japanese recommendation, a proposal has been put forth to organise several influential businessmen and politicians into a body called the 'Northeastern Industrial Development Commission' that might guide Fengtian's industrial development.
Expand the Anshan Mines
The enormous iron deposits in Anshan have been described as being of 'world class significance', and churn out nearly 7 million tonnes of iron, with the potential to triple output by 1942. This expansion seems likely to propel Anshan toward becoming one of East Asia's largest industrial centres.
Establish the Jinzhou Industrial Zone
Jinzhou's docks and strategic position in the 'Liaoxi Corridor', which connects land transportation between North and Northeast China, make it a prime target for government incentivised development. It remains to be seen whether special rules will be applied to this zone favouring Chinese or Japanese companies.
Expand the Fushun Mines
The mines around Fushun churn out nearly 11 million tons of coal per year, with deposits promising to produce over 4.5 billion tonnes total. While some modern trains and ships in the West use oil, the Japanese Empire runs on coal, and the strategic significance of these mines cannot be understated.
Yingkou Commercial Development
The port city of Yingkou serves as Fengtian's primary gateway to the world, and the second largest port on the Bohai Gulf after Japanese-controlled [745.GetCapitalVictoryPointName]. The tremendous increase in material production in Fengtian demands an equally large investment in commercial infrastructure.
Develop the Three Northeast Provinces
The Three Northeast Provinces, Fengtian, Jilin, and Heilongjiang, already contain over 30% of China's railroads and much of its heavy industry. However, if the National Reclamation War is to be won, both will have to be expanded upon and improved. Ideally this would be achieved solely by the Chinese people, but reality dictates that the Japanese will lead much of the path forward.
Wang Yongjiang's Legacy
Manchuria's transformation from a backward borderland into one of China's most prosperous regions owes itself to the work of Wang Yongjiang, Zhang Zuolin's late Finance Minister. Disgusted by the Grand Marshal's costly excursions south of the Great Wall in 1928, Wang resigned and died shortly thereafter, his work left unfinished. We must pick up where he left off.
Reorganise the NTC
Founded by the Fengtian Government shortly after its creation, the National Transportation Commission serves as a planning board for infrastructure construction across the country. The Japanese allege that its foremost aim is to disrupt Mantetsu's operations, and there may be at least some truth to this claim.
Support Sino-Japanese Joint Companies
A great number of businesses in Fengtian offer shares to both Chinese and Japanese, including the infamous Mantetsu, but relatively few Chinese have the funds to invest and as a result most joint companies are Japanese dominated. Government backing may permit us to provide means and incentives to fellow Chinese and gradually shift this balance.
From Beijing to the Begonia Leaf
For decades, students and nationalists have compared the shape of China, that is to say China undivided, to the shape of a Begonia leaf. With Beijing in our hands, it has come time to reclaim all of our homeland, and make the Begonia Leaf a reality!
Suppress the Bandits; Collect the Harvest
The last time soldiers of the Fengtian Army entered the North China Plain, some units were encouraged to suppress banditry and assist in collection the seasonal harvest in return for lodgings and food. Where such amenities were normally simply seized, these tactics seem to have ameliorated local unrest and partisan activity. All commanders would do well to follow this example.
Continue the Reclamation War
The war of National Reclamation did not end with the capture of Beijing. One by one, each of China's provinces must be brought to heel, and the country once again unified.
Integrate Occupied Arsenals
The Shenyang Arsenal is unquestionably the greatest in China, but by integrating and specialising newly seized arsenals, now as part of a national supply system, we may be able to ease the burden on Shenyang and improve our overall logistical capability.
Crush Flies and Capture Pigs
Corruption and abuse of power have run rampant throughout China over the past several decades, and all levels of the Fengtian Government are complicit in this activity. In order to regain the public's trust, some measure of law and order must be restored, and examples will be made of both low-level “Flies” and high-level “Pigs”, who have been greedily gorging themselves on the nation's livelihood.
Expand the Baojia System
The Baojia System is an ancient method of social organisation and military recruitment. Zhang Zuolin revived the practice several decades ago in the Northeast, and to great effect, but now the time has come to once again expand the system to the rest of China, where it has by and large fallen by the wayside.
Incorporate Local Patronage Networks
There is more to every institution than meets the eye, and every good warlord builds his stronghold through a network of reciprocal partnerships negotiated behind closed doors. With the collapse of enemy authority, there are many such individuals and institutions without a clear place in the new order. There is every reason to begin incorporating these individuals into our own networks, where possible.
Centralise Provincial Revenues
Perhaps the greatest source of disunity in China has been the decentralisation of the tax system, begun with the introduction of provincial “Lijin” transit tariffs in 1853. The new Central Government must limit provincial taxation, and reduce the percentage local authorities may keep for themselves. Otherwise, local governments will continue to deny the nation revenue.
Institute Labour Discipline
The industrial policy of our nation is being threatened by the increasingly divergent interests of industrialists, union leaders and workers. Unions serve only to divide, and creating distrust, forcing the leaders of our country to compromise. Only through an intervention that solidifies the discipline and loyalty of labour organisations, can the unity be forged that will allow us to move our country forward.
The Generals Know Best
There is no doubt that a centralised army can serve as the foundation to a centralised state, but China's great size requires a different approach. For this reason, we will continue to appoint military governors. To better balance this arrangement, provincial armies must recruit the majority of troops from outside their own provinces, and limit their production and deployment of heavy weapons.
One Army One Republic
If we are to learn a single lesson from over two thousand years of Chinese history, it is that when military force is divided, so too is the country. In order to build a unified China we must create a single army, beneath a single banner, at the direction of a single command structure. This measure will not be popular at any level of government outside the Cabinet.
Secure the Rear Areas
The North China Plain has been seized, but it has not been pacified. For now, the Army controls only the railways and their immediate proximity, with bandits and partisans running wild beyond. China is a big country, and the rear areas must be thoroughly scoured in order to ensure an uncompromised advance toward the goal of national reunification.
Against Imperialism of All Forms
Japan poses itself as a friend, an able ally, perhaps even an equal. But the Chinese know better; their designs on the nation, their aspirations for Asia as a whole, their deriding attitude towards detachment from their Chinese \
Faith in the Anguojun
Only the National Pacification Army, the military arm of the Fengtian-led rival government, can guarantee the legacy of the Xinhai Revolution and the Five Races Under One Union. Sullied by the likes of provincial warlords, Federalists, Third-Way Democrats, and Revolutionaries, the Chinese Revolution has been terribly distorted, turned into a feral cancer that must be pacified. And it is only our officers that are capable of such.
Ensuring Efficient Procurement
Keen to fatten themselves and guarantee their own futures, the various petty warlords and minor bandits have found themselves seizing \
Revitalise the Bank of Communications
The Bank of Communications once held the very stability of Chinese government cabinets in its palms, for it facilitiated foreign investments, crucially to back the governments of Yuan Shikai, and later that of Duan Qirui. Yet with the Nishiwara Loan and the outcry of the Paris Peace Conference, it has been far diminished. It is only natural that its clerk's capabilities once more be exhibited in a primary role.
Renewing Trust in Industry
With a nigh-unending Warlord Era, bar a brief interregnum of Zhili Unification, the stability and faith within the Chinese nation-state's industrial capacity is particularly lacklustre, at least as far as foreign firms are concerned. With an explosion of Anti-Concessionism off the cusp of the Shanghai Uprising and other events, it will take a concerted government effort to restore faith in our factories.
The Marshal and the Emperor
Hand-in-hand, the Son of Heaven and the Old Marshal of Dongbei have marched forward onto a new era of prosperity for Asia. It would be amiss to end things prematurely. Whatever Fengtian needs, it receives from Japan, and whilst many in the government warn the Marshal of traps, intrigues, and plots linked to the Japanese, it takes more than a simple spy to kill the Tiger of the North.
Following the Kingly Way
The Kingly Way, that Confucian method of governance to ensure morality and benevolence, whilst traditionally applied to the Emperor in respect to his court, finds much a similar place within the Marshal's Palace. Make no mistake, there shall be no monarchs in the new China, but the Old Marshal, the Father of the Nation, it is his portrait on Tiananmen Square, and it is to his example of which the Chinese must emulate.
Militarise the Student Body
In this period of great strife and terrible bloodshed, it is the youth whom suffer most. Deprived of the most basic building blocks of their future, the education system, they can all but languish as the nation grows increasingly wounded. But it is the same youth that hold the nation's future in their palms, and it is their duty to fight for China, and for national liberation.
Dictatorship of the Transport Ministry
Railways bring prosperity! Or well, they should have. Yet most railways within China are built by Western companies, or at the very least funded by them. In a practical sense, they have always been a symbol of simultaneous progress, yet abounding imperialism. Through decisive action, men such as Chang Yinhuai will reclaim the railways from the imperialist, and return them to the Central Government's fold.
Dongbei's Final Victory
After numerous failed attempts over a span of over a decade, Fengtian has finally triumphed above all of its enemies; the Zhili, Anhui, or the Russians, none could withstand the ingenuity and skill of Dongbei's sons and daughters. With the securing of Beijing for a third time, all that is left is to decide upon the future of the Chinese Republic, and many lives may hang in such a balance.

From Poverty to Extravagance
Having once been a mere bandit roaming the wastes of the Three Northeastern Provinces, Zhang Zuolin has ascended far beyond even the greatest dreams of the most minor bandit. Not only a Grand Marshal, but that of the kingmaker of the whole nation. It is he of which the army responds to, almost, his every beck and call, and it is to Zhang Zuolin of which the Republic owes Ten Thousand Years!
Commencing True Recovery
Squabbling amongst themselves for over half a decade, it would appear that the Recovery League has finally received the Green Light to consolidate itself, and its political gains. Having been the main outfit by which the Fengtian Clique exerted its political ambitions, the re-appointment of Pan Fu to the position as Prime Minister has consolidated the vision of the Republic as a vessel for advancement.
Harmonising the Social Classes
The masses are a powerful force, capable of a political whirlwind few associations can withstand; Anhui realised this, perhaps only in hindsight. But one can curry favour with the masses, without becoming beholden to them. By building strength between the peasantry, workers, gentry, and industrialists, China can bring forward new prosperity almost entirely upon its own strength.
The First Party of the State
There is no other association, league, party, or group that can fathom being capable of rulership within China. This is a beast that is entirely unbeknownst to most other men in the field. We are not Apostles of Democracy, nor are we naive enough to continue autocracy, we present the only solution for the eventual attainment of civic rights, welfare, education, and stability.
Clear-Cut Political Economics
This is not a game of cards, the life of all Chinese are at stake, and the Central Government cannot be entrusted to transform its most humble villages and hamlets into modern cities if its rulers are merely politicians. Only under men of business wit and capability can China be assured of economic development and progress. It can only be hoped that ten years from now, China will become a metropolis.
Alliance of State and Business
The true keys to China's recovery after decades of disunity and disruption is that of capital, and it is only through the men of capital, and their assets, that the government can produce the necessary means to connect China at its fraying seams. By engaging in government contracts with various major companies, they make rake in the benefits, whilst the government can direct their resources to proper usage.
Government As a Machine
There can be no time for debate or pettyness in statecraft; ideology, intellectualism, and idealism, they merely serve to dissuade advancing efforts of the government to perform its duties at maximum efficiency. The government is the only vessel by which the nation can reclaim itself on the world stage, and it as such it should be run like a machine, or a factory, based on profits at little cost.
The President of Providence
A man of duty, of perseverance, of servitude and of loyalty, Yang Yuting has long been denied his destiny. And it is most blatantly out of fear for his capabilities. Having fought for most of the Warlord Era, he would only find himself deprived of positions due to the meddling of men like Xueliang. But now they pose no threat to the Man of Providence, and his revitalised Republic.
The Dragon's Gambit
Few would believe that any one man could corral or control the Fengtian Clique as remotely well as the Old Marshal, but then those men have not met Yang Yuting or Chang Yinhuai. Playing the same game, but coming out on top, Yang has produced his greatest gambit yet. There will no longer be a facade of niceties or the incompetence of Xueliang to dash his desires. May the Five Races fly forever high!
Redeeming the Lost Patriots
With tacit connections from the 1920s, Yang has always maintained a close eye of admiration and curiosity in regards to the Young China Party. Whilst unable to truly associate with them in the Northeast, in-part due to their anti-Fengtian oppositional stance, and Feng Yong's alignment with Xueliang, now that they are face-to-face, Yang must but only open his arms to his new set of skilled scholars.
The Rising Sun and the Waking Tiger
Zhang Zuolin thought himself capable of arranging an agreement of equals with the Japanese, but he lacked the tact or skills required to produce such an arrangement. Yang Yuting however, far more capable as a soldier, orator, and politician, has managed to win genuine favour from Tokyo. No longer are they master and subject, but true equals, and together, undefeatable.

Freedom of the Five Races
China is a nation of many nationalities: Han, Manchu, Mongolian, Tibetan, Hui. And even such a delineation is hardly thorough and all-encompassing. By uniting the various nationalities of China through the guiding concepts of the Kingly Way, the state can bind national harmony to the very concept of citizenship and statehood; a nation of morality, and etiquette, not revolution.
The Chinese Shogunate
Simply put, the Qing refused to modernise due to their own arrogance and perception of celestial rights; despite numerous overtures from various states that offered immensely beneficial deals, the court would always run to obstruct modernisation. But the men of China today are far more pragmatic; if we can learn everything from Japan, we will inevitably become stronger than them.
In the Spirit of 1912
Perhaps out of folly, idealism, or a faint desire for a more utopian world, the North and South have once again attempted a mutually beneficial deal of national unification. Retaining the various Southern Federal Governors, alongside the appointment of Zhang Junmai as Prime Minister, perhaps it will go smoother than last time.
