Found the Shenyang National Academy
In the years of economic hardship following the last Zhifeng War, the Northeastern Army Lecture Hall began to stagnate. By refounding the old academy under a new name and updating its curriculum, it can again become a point of pride.
Promote Young Officers
Despite years of reform, our officer corps still suffers from a chronic lack of modern thinking with a significant portion of the officer corps being made up of older sub-par officers. While both the Shikan Clique and Shaoshuai Clique have different candidates for promotion, they nevertheless both advocate for the promotion of young, talented officers. Let us heed their advice to eleviate our current leadership problems.
Obtain Japanese Instructors
The Japanese field a modern military and industrial sector comparable in strength and discipline with any in the West. Given that the Japanese government is willing to provide instructors free of charge, we should take this opportunity to build a force our enemies will envy.
Modernised Curriculum
The modern Japanese curriculum, designed to counter Russian aggression on the plains of Manchuria, emphasises morale factors and tenacity of the will, stressing training designed to develop the ability to recognise opportunities for decisive attack; enveloping open enemy flanks, encircling formations, and thus destroying numerically and technologically superior forces.
Improve our Logistics
Our logistics network has always been one of the best in China. Since the First Zhili-Anhui war our logistics system has been able to funnel supplies and reinforcements quickly and efficiently to the frontline, allowing us to effectively utilise our large industrial and manpower base to our advantage. Let us once again utilise this advantage against our enemies!
Modernise Infantry Tactics
During the last few conflicts we have been involved in, our infantry have been found lacking in multiple aspects. Our machine gunners were operating off outdated tactics, often with unskilled gunners. Our infantry often found themselves unsupported by artillery and other support weapons. If we hope to emerge victorious in our upcoming struggle to unite China, we must modernise our infantry tactics and fix any remaining issues we may have.
Utilise our Strengths
Over the last two decades our artillery force was one of the bright spots within our often lacklustre army, with their effective and often accurate fire helping us emerge victorious in many battles. While the two Young Guard factions have differing ideas on how our artillery corps should operate moving forward, they both agree that maintaining a strong artillery arm will be a deciding factor of our upcoming wars. Let us continue to utilise this strength.
Collaborative Equipment Design
By partnering with Japanese manufacturers to create and streamline designs suited to the unique Chinese environment, we can produce superior weapons at a lower cost. This may make us reliant on expensive Japanese-built machinery, but in the long run we will have the tools we need to pacify all of China.
Turn to the Youngsters
Led by Zhang Xueliang, the Shaoshuai Clique arose after our defeat in the Third Zhili Fengtian war. Comprised mainly of young forward thinking officers, they emphasise the need for a well disciplined core of NCOs and infantrymen. Therefore, we must entrust our army reform to these young officers and their old guard allies so that we can prepare ourselves for the inevitable confrontation with our enemies in the south while also staving Japanese influence in our army.
Train New Field Officers
Historically, the Fengtian Army had found itself lacking skilled junior officers capable of maintaining cohesion at the front lines. By training a new generation of field officers, we can distribute skilled junior officers to our entire army and both aleviate the our shortage of skilled leadership and ensure our troops will continue to be effective at a tactical level.
Promote New NCOs
Drawing from teachings at the Baoding military academy and the influence of Guo Songling, the Shaoshuai Clique emphasises the need for a capable corps of NCOs to maintain the cohesion and discipline of our troops at the front lines. By promoting promising soldiers into these positions, our armies can hope to defeat the enemy through superior discipline and organisation instead of solely relying on our superior equipment as we have done historically.
Model Soldiers
While our army has come a long way since our defeat in 1922, our significant portion of our forces are still comprised of unmotivated and poorly trained troops. Therefore, we must mandate our troops undergo rigourous physical and combat training, as well as moral indoctrination, in order to create a skilled, disciplined and motivated fighting force that would match any army in China.
Mobilise the People
As we have done during our many conflicts up to this point, we must draw from the Northeast's rich industrial and manpower bases in order to effectively supply our armies with arms and fresh recruits.
Legacy of Guo Songling
Despite Guo Songling's treachery his legacy within the Fengtian army is hard to ignore, particularly his influence with our younger officers. However, his ideas have proved to be quite effective in the years following his death and has lead our army to many victories. Perhaps by adopting and refining his ideas, as well as returning his followers to more influential positions, we can greatly increase our army's strength.
Modernise the Cavalry
Historically, our cavalry force has performed exceptionally well in the North China Plain against our adversaries. During the Second Zhili-Fengtian War, our cavalry proved to be a vital part of our victor in Rehe. We must ensure our cavalry force is up to modern standards if we hope to replicate our previous successes. Furthermore, General Ma Zhanshan has suggested that our cavalry may also prove useful in the event our enemies occupy our lands...
Learn From the Russians
After witnessing the awesome power of railway artillery and armoured trains being used by our Russian neighbours, both during their civil war and their infrequent border clashes with our own army and Japanese forces, many within our clique have been convinced of the effectiveness of railway artillery. While expensive, they may prove invaluable in breaching powerful fortifications built by our enemies to the south.
Turn to the Shikan Clique
The Shikan Clique, lead by Yang Yuting, are a group of officers educated at the Rikugun Shikan Gakko in Japan. Yang's goals of creating a centralised command structure, precision artillery strikes and modern officer corps have served us well in the past, especially on the Rehe front during the Second Zhili-Fengtian War. Perhaps Yang Yuting's ideas can once again transform the Fengtian army into one of the greatest armies in China.

Lessons of the Weltkrieg
While we formally participated in the Weltkrieg on the side of the Entente, we only witnessed the carnage caused by modern weaponry and tactics from afar, through both observers and associates within the Japanese military. We can hope to greatly improve our army's combat effectiveness if we take the lessons learned by the great powers to heart by emphasising the need for a skilled engineer and artillery corps.
Study Japanese Infantry Tactics
During the very limited Japanese interventions by the Imperial Japanese Military in our conflicts, their tactics have proved to be extremely effective. Their infantry in particular have proven to be extremely capable in infiltration assault operations leading to many victories. Learning from these Japanese strategies may prove extremely useful for our army's combat effectiveness.
A New Generation of Chinese Officers
If we are to produce one of the premier fighting forces in China, our officers must match the standards of our new army. Therefore, our new generation of Chinese officers must be disciplined, knowledgeable and loyal to us if we are to produce skilled officers who will be fit to lead our new army.
A Modern General Staff
Much of the Imperial Japanese Army's success can be traced back to their general staff. Therefore, to replicate their successes we must create a modern general staff of our own, allowing us to create battle plans for any confrontation with our enemies long before we come to blows. Consequently, this would give us an advantage over our enemies and would prove extremely useful in our battles against our southern adversaries.
A Methodical Approach to War
After observing the past three decades of almost constant fighting, only one conclusion can be drawn. Even in China, where armies hundreds of thousands strong regularly clash with one another, fanaticism and numbers will not win battles. Only a strong, elite and modern force backed by modern strategy will win us battles. Therefore, we must adopt a methodical approach to war to ensure that our armies can emerge victorious.

Rearm the Northeast
The Shenyang Arsenal was once China's greatest military-industrial enterprise, but the past decade has seen it eclipsed by the combined production of other Chinese arsenals, such as those at Hanyang, Baoding, and Jiangnan. We must reclaim our place at the top, and in doing so reduce our reliance on Japanese military aid. We can begin by stamping out corruption and increasing production quotas.
Diversify Armament Production
The Shenyang Arsenal has always been a massive but totally centralised operation, with one single plant and sub-factories in the Shenyang area accounting for the entirety of the Northeast's armament production. Eventually, size becomes a burden. We must consider diversifying our equipment manufacturing process to include components built at separate plants, or even by private companies.
Zaibatsu Investments
By opening our armaments industry to the Zaibatsu we are inevitably inviting increased Japanese influence in Manchuria. However, they can provide more money than we could ever afford to spend, and their manufacturing processes are far more sophisticated than our own.
Jigyou Hikaku
The Japanese have recommended that our military-industrial enterprises adopt a strategy of comparing business results, or 'Jigyou Hikaku', in which proprietary data on production is disclosed. They will then rank performance and dispatch consultants to improve our industrial methods. This should boost production, though it will give the Japanese plenty of information about our military industry.
Expand the Shenyang Arsenal
China's largest military-industrial enterprise through the 1920s, the enormous Shenyang Arsenal produces a wide variety of modified small arms and artillery, usually based around designs acquired from overseas. By expanding its operations and introducing newer equipment we can substantially increase its output.
Develop the Dadong Artillery Complex
[FNG.GetLeader] has always had an enthusiasm for big guns, and the Mukden Arsenal has always built its artillery at the Shenyang Mortar Factory in Dadong; a northeastern district of Shenyang. By expanding this operation into a totally separate artillery complex, we can maximise its efficiency.
The Kwantung Protocol
In light of the growing friendship between our two nations, the Kwantung Army has petitioned Japan's Army Ministry to increase cooperation. This is set to include the transfer of weapons and technology, as well as training. All we need to do is add our signature to the prepared document, though accepting will play straight into the hands of the Concordia Association.
Reorganise the Coastal Defence Forces
Because the Fengtian Navy has no realistic way of opposing the larger and newer navy fielded by [QIE.GetNameDef], its main purpose is coastal defence. In light of recent troubling inadequacies, such as one ship's crew selling their armament on the black market, extensive reorganisation and reform is necessary.
Expand Yingkou Naval Yard
Yingkou is the Northeast Region's second-largest port, after Japanese-held [745.GetCapitalVictoryPointName], and the home of our Navy. If we are to begin any meaningful naval reconstruction project, expansion of the Yingkou Naval Yard is an essential first step.
The Nine Points Strategy
The severe asymmetry in strength between the Fengtian and [QIE.GetAdjective] navies means that, in the absence of Japanese support, our entire coast will be at risk of invasion. Japanese strategists have outlined nine positions at which naval landings are most likely, and drafted plans for their defence.
Regular River Patrols
The Navy possesses number of small patrol boats, occasionally used to police the Yalu and Songhua rivers, but the majority of which are currently rusting away in storage. These might be better used to train our crews and maintain our internal security, if we can find the funding.
Re-Forming the Marine Corps
A marine corps was created in 1914, called the 'Republic of China Marine Corps,' but this attempt went nowhere. We will revive the China Marine Corps along modern lines, enabling us to better operate in riverine environments like the Huang He and Yangtze. Given the right opportunity, we may even be able to cross the Bohai Sea, and make Wu Peifu's old strategy our own.
Commission Japanese Ships
There can be no doubt that our own ship-building capabilities pale compared to those of the Imperial Japanese Navy. They will never give us the ships necessary to build a truly modern fleet, but they might sell us enough to make a difference against other Chinese, and any other future threats.
Request Japanese Airframes
While we have a strong air force in comparison to most warlords, our air force still lacks behind the [QIE.GetName] air force in size and modernity, as they are supplied with modern German aircraft. We will need to leverage our relationship to Japan in order to be able to have a chance against them.
Restructure the China Flying Corps
Originally organised by the Grand Marshal's son, Zhang Xueliang, the Corps performed well in the last war, losing air superiority only upon the arrival of more modern German-piloted planes. Since then it's expanded, but retains aircraft decades behind Western standards.
Request Aircraft Blueprints
True aircraft design requires well educated and extremely specialised engineers, which we sadly don't have access to. As a result, in order to improve our air force, we must order more from Japan.
Reverse Engineering Efforts
With some Japanese planes in our possession, it seems possible that we might reverse engineer them for our own use, though the success of such efforts cannot be guaranteed.
Shoutai Tactics
Enormous advances in aircraft design in recent years have produced planes that fly completely differently than their predecessors, requiring reevaluations of flight manoeuvring and tactics. The Japanese have reorganised their Air Squadrons into three-plane 'Shoutai' units which are designed around the flexibility necessary for dogfighting. These could give us an important edge.
Expand the Shenyang Aerodrome
One of China's first military aviation centres, the Shenyang Aerodrome requires expansion in-line with our increasing air power.
Once the greatest of the Beiyang warlords and master of Northern China, the Fengtian Clique found itself reduced to its base in the Northeast by a resurgent Zhili Clique and was left sole heir to the Xinhai Revolution following the Qing Restoration.\n\nBalancing internal factions with ever-growing Japanese influence, Marshal Zhang rebuilds his army for one final struggle against his Zhili rivals. Will the Old Marshal successfully march into the Central Plains and carry out unification, or will his benefactors in Tokyo crush the Chinese dream underfoot?

The Bastion in the North
As the year 1936 dawns, Fengtian stands in the Northeast as the final bastion of China's Republican dream. As with many things in China however, the abstractions of this dream hide complex and often inconvenient truths. The Fengtian Government of the Republic of China, contesting [QIE.GetNameDef]'s claims to legitimacy, maintains democracy only as a thin veneer, covering what has always been, and perhaps always will be, an authoritarian state.\n\nThe Assembly in Shenyang is widely regarded to be corrupt, power divided between autocratic generals, unscrupulous railway barons, and Pan-Asianist ideologues with questionable motivations. Amid it all stands Grand Marshal Zhang Zuolin, his ambitions great, but limited by the stark realities of [QIE.GetAdjective] strength and Japanese power; for now forced to walk a political tightrope between the two, and above the machinations of his own divided government. The status quo cannot last forever, and if the right moment to strike south is not chosen soon, it may never come at all.\n\nThe staggering cost of the wars with the south and the severance of economic ties left Fengtian reeling, and while past years have been spent rebuilding, there is much left to do. Likewise, the army has suffered from neglect, and must be reorganised. The Japanese, their influence growing by the day, present both a dire threat and an opportunity. The waters ahead are treacherous, and it will take a truly great helmsman to steer the ship of state not only to survival, but also toward the reclamation of all China.\n\nBriefings are available on Fengtian's special mechanics, its relationship with the Japanese, and internal politics.
Special Mechanics Briefing
The Fengtian Government is unstable, pressured from without and within, ultimately a fusion of elements that would be contradictory were it not for their shared goals. The parties, more accurately termed factions, exercise their grip through dominance of the country's institutions instead of mass appeal. As such, the 'popularity' of parties should be taken to represent their degree of control over the country's government and other structures of power, control being determined not by the popular policies of ministers, but by choices, focuses, and events that increase or diminish their power.\n\nConsequently, your aim should be to balance the various factions, each of which has the potential to abuse their power if given too much of it, though each will do so differently. Each political advisor is part of one of the four factions. Each advisor hired, in addition to their trait, will improve the Divided Governance national spirit while also boosting the influence of their respective faction. As such, advisors should be picked wisely to avoid the negative consequences of an imbalance of power later down the line.\n\nAnother crucial point is the role of our benefactors in Tokyo, whose influence grows and wanes in the Fengtian Clique depending on our reliance on their aid. As their influence grows, it will lead to increasing bonuses to production, but at the cost of political power and autonomy. The rise of this influence is inevitable over time, and should be viewed with caution.
Japanese Briefing
The Japanese exercise their power in Fengtian through a series of treaties permitting them not only extraterritoriality, but also the right to live and work in Fengtian more or less as if they were its citizens. While the Grand Marshal and others utilise a wide variety of means to slow and inconvenience the Japanese, their presence is necessary and the growth of their influence inevitable. The primary institution responsible for this growth is the South Manchuria Railway Company, more commonly termed 'Mantetsu', the profits from which in recent years have accounted for nearly a quarter of Japan's entire national budget.\n\nAt the same time, the Japanese need Fengtian and what it represents. Its cooperation and the prospect of a victory in the South offer to save Japan a great deal of time and money. The result is a tenuous balance, the Japanese ever looking for more profit and power, but well aware that pushing too hard will place Zhang Zuolin in a politically untenable position, and thus bring their careful efforts to naught.\n\nSo far Zhang has pursued a patchwork policy; promotion of Pan-Asian brotherhood with Japan, only to intermittently replace this with repudiations of Japanese initiatives that push too far, and consistent private efforts to lessen Japanese influence. How to proceed will be your choice, but caution is advised.
Politics Briefing
Fengtian has four primary political factions:\n\n1. The Recovery League\n\nA loose association of fallen generals, governors, bureaucrats, and politicians without any strong ideological affiliation, most of whom find themselves in Fengtian because there are few other places where they might hold any semblance of power. Easily bribed and tempted, they often serve to promote the interests of whoever is willing to pay, and consequently the 'league' is highly splintered despite controlling a large portion of the Assembly, lacking the political will to act decisively.\n\n2. The Zhang Clique\n\nA collection of loyalists and generals, the Zhang Clique holds no specific ideology beyond promoting the furtherance of the Grand Marshal's political powers. While making pretences to democracy, Zhang's supporters are not committed to republican ideals, and promote them only for their utility.\n\n3. The Communications Clique\n\nThe sole politically coherent faction to emerge from the former Beiyang Government, the Communications Clique are a collection of railroad and telegraph barons, primarily self-interested, but locked in confrontation with Mantetsu and the Concordia Association over the country's infrastructure.\n\n4. Japanese Influence\n\nA collection of bureaucrats and officers from Japan sent to Shenyang ostensibly to aid Marshal Zhang Zuolin, these men represent various interests in the service of Tokyo. The Kwantung Army hopes to maintain Manchuria's autonomy from the rest of China, the Tianjin Army seeks to assist the Fengtian reclamation of China in order to expand Japanese influence across all of China, and the various Japanese bureaucrats hope to test new policies deemed radical in the Home Islands.

Rumours Incite Regionalist Uproar
Although no plans have been made public, or even exist in anything approaching a final form, rumours have already begun to spread that the Fengtian Army is preparing to march south and conquer Beijing within the next month. The scattered news coming in from the south has inspired a potent mix of excitement and concern, and confrontations have already broken out in tea rooms, bars, and other public places between ardent nationalists and regionalist 'Dongbei Party' members.\n\nThe 'Dongbei Party' is not a political party in any real sense, and more a nickname applied by detractors to any espousing doubts about Zhang Zuolin's mission to reunite the country. A significant number of local officials and bureaucrats, including school teachers, share this kind of scepticism and have begun organising protests criticising what they view as a costly and unnecessary war.\n\nNaturally, the government will not refute the rumours, as that might free up Beijing's hand to intervene in the League Crisis.
Rumours can be dangerous...
Regionalists Take Action
Shouting 'Dongbei weile Dongbeiren' or 'The Northeast for Northeastern People', protestors have gathered near the Grand Marshal's palace, in Harbin's Sophia Square, and outside Jilin's Medical College demanding an end to war preparations. Their numbers are not great enough to present serious problems, and police have already been dispatched to maintain order, but this is only part of an ongoing campaign which threatens to undermine public confidence in the regime. If the whole of the Northeast cannot be united behind the Grand Marshal's dream to reunite all of China, then how can it ever be realised?
Protestors gathered again in several prominent locations in Northeastern cities. Their numbers were not great enough to present serious problems, but that did not stop police from cracking down hard, wading into the masses with clubs and rifle butts, and scattering fleeing protestors into crowded side streets. Angered by the violence, some 'Dongbei Party' members have already vowed to return in even greater numbers, but it is hoped that this quick and decisive response will deter all but the movement's hard-liners, making them all the easier to round-up and silence.\n\nMore concerning is talk among members of local trade associations, chambers of commerce, and town assemblies of a tax boycott. Unlike some of the young students, these older men remember the hard times late last decade when war expenditures outgrew the Northeastern economy and sent it into economic freefall.
Despite efforts by the police regionalist protests have continued sporadically across the Northeast, and have been given further weight by support from local chambers of commerce, currency exchanges, and other business institutions concerned about the economic costs of a war to the south. While this currently appears to be posturing, there is no telling whether these groups will undermine the war-effort when the decisive moment comes, and while the public protests have yet to turn violent it may be only a matter of time. The sooner this problem is addressed the better.
News of continued conflicts to the south have given the regionalist movement renewed momentum. Attempts at suppression have been continually hampered by the unwillingness of some sympathetic bureaucrats, police chiefs, and other officials to carry out their duties in full. Undoubtedly a complete effort will need to be made to root out these frustrating elements and restore order. As the public discontent continues the legitimacy and strength of our government is gradually sapped away.
Unfortunate.
Agent Provocateurs in Action
Just as planned, our well-placed agents have successfully pushed some in the regionalist movement toward violence. Already increasingly violent protests have caused damage to public property, and reactions have been negative. It may only be a matter of time before we have the justification we need.
Excellent.
The Harbin Riots
A protest rapidly escalated into an all-out riot last night, as protestors clashed with police in downtown Harbin. There have been fifteen recorded deaths, with unknown numbers of wounded on both sides, numbers possibly stretching into the low hundreds. Of particular concern is the Harbin Central Station which saw its front windows shattered, and its roof in flames. Damage to the station and several pieces of rolling stock have delayed travel along connecting rail lines, and the bureaucrats at Mantetsu have already registered their outrage.\n\nCleaning up this mess may take some time, but at least we now have a clear justification for action against the regionalist movement.
Good... and bad.
Mass Arrests Begin
With the appropriate justification now in place, our dutiful police officers, with support from local militia and the Fengtian Army, have begun rounding up suspected protestors. The majority will eventually be sent home, but not necessarily in one piece. Hopefully, their imprisonment will serve as a message to the other protestors, and any sympathisers, that the government will no longer tolerate their subversion.
Good riddance.
An Offer from the Kempeitai
The Kempeitai, the Japanese Army's extrajudicial police force, have taken note of our regionalist problem and come forward with a partial solution. With a wide network of informants, they claim to have information on a number of figures underpinning the regionalist movement - information they have volunteered. In response, we must provide intelligence on several anti-Japanese agitators and insurgents who have so far slipped through their fingers; not in the least due to our own interference. So far it has been convenient for us to keep in contact with these nationalists, pending cases where we need to push back against Japanese influence.\n\nIs this one of those cases? Or should we take the deal and offer these people up on a silver platter?
Take the deal.
No thank you.
Regionalist Movement Suppressed
The 'Dongbei Party', and the regionalist movement in general, have been suppressed at last. While this is not an end to regionalist sentiment in the Northeast, it may last for decades to come, but for now it has ceased to be a consideration as we turn our attention southward.
Progress.
Picking up the Educational Slack
Our targeted removal of regionalist 'Dongbei Party' school teachers and other intellectuals has predictably led to educational chaos and major research interruptions, but staffers at the Japanese Consulate have come forward with a possible solution. Mantetsu has long maintained a series of privately run schools originally intended for the sons and daughters of employees, as well as Japanese immigrants, which pride themselves on providing an education comparable to or even exceeding those available in the Home Islands. At our behest, the Japanese government might pressure Mantetsu to open these to the public and provide staff to fill temporary shortages.\n\nOnce we open the door to this kind of activity it will be very difficult to close, and these schools will almost certainly be used to spread Japanese culture and norms. We should consider carefully.
Decline the offer.
Accept the offer.
The Kimono Scandal
Scandal! In a most unfortunate turn of events, the Grand Marshal's youngest daughter has been photographed wearing a Japanese Kimono during a photo-session at the Mantetsu-run 'Hokutō Kokuritsudaigaku' or 'Northeast National Academy'. Despite risk of arrest, word of the photo has already spread widely, along with a few copies of the image itself, though local and national news agencies know better than to print this defamation. Some agents in the military's intelligence branch speculate that the image was intentionally taken and spread by the Japanese as a means of punishing the government for recent actions, but no supporting evidence has emerged.\n\nThere is little question, however, that our enemies will use this opportunity to spread their nefarious propaganda.
What an embarrassment!
Close the Mantetsu schools!
Students Join the Youth League
In an embarrassing and deeply damaging incident, a band of Chinese school children from Changchun recently announced their intention to join the Fengtian Youth League, which actively promotes Japanese interests in our country. Obviously their young minds are easily impressionable, but their parade through the streets of their home city, waving Japanese flags, has disgusted many and invited outright enmity toward the government. Parents weep, asking how their children could become so warped, and demand an alternative to these dangerous Japanese-run schools.
This is an outrage!
Close the schools!
Chinese Uniforms for Chinese Students
After the demoralising effects of our harsh but necessary crack-down on 'Dongbei Party' teachers, our Education Ministry has come forward with a new national school uniform. While this may seem like a small change, the uniforms are a symbol of Chinese independence and national identity stretching beyond any particular region. Surely a bright new future awaits our students as part of a united China!
A point of pride!
Developing Infrastructure in Liaoning
Northeast China's infrastructure is often considered superior to what can be found across the rest of the country, but even so it rarely meets western standards. For all their modernity, Mantetsu's railways fail to fully cover a region the size of France and Germany combined. Smaller provincial rail lines, as well as a network of criss-crossing motorways, have been built over past decades in an attempt to solve this problem, but they are few and far between - not to mention often poorly maintained. If we are to stimulate economic development, and better support our armies in the field, we must further develop these networks and ensure their maintenance. Liaoning, the heart of our operations, is as good a place to start as any, and a collection of smaller Chinese companies are already eager to begin work.\n\nThese companies, in the absence of Mantetsu and Japanese engineers, will do a great deal to demonstrate Chinese strength and independence.

Infrastructure Development in Liaoning Complete
After months of construction and various unfortunate delays, the planned infrastructure developments in Liaoning ares finally complete. After reviewing plans and available resources, the NTC will undoubtedly make another contract available soon.
Great news!
Developing Infrastructure in Liaobei and Jilin
In contrast to Liaoning, existing local infrastructure in Liaobei and Jilin is somewhat sparse, particularly in the foothills of the Greater Khingan and Changbai ranges. The NTC has drafted an elaborate Japanese-inspired plan intended to link the central hubs of Jilin City and Changchun to otherwise isolated communities, with road extending outward almost like spokes on a wheel. The plan is so extensive that much of it is beyond our ability to complete in a reasonable time-frame, and such we will be completing only its initial stages for now.

Developing Infrastructure in Nenjiang and Songjiang
While far more tame than the wilds of Heilongjiang or the Hailar Steppe, Nenjiang and Songjiang represent some of the least developed areas in Manchuria. The majority of our work there will mean transforming ancient footpaths, winding across hills and between mountains, into modern narrow-gauge railways or sturdy motorways. By necessity, most of our work will link up to the 'Chinese Eastern Railway', originally built by the Russians as part of the Trans-Siberian railway, but now heavily influenced by the Japanese.

Infrastructure Development in Nenjiang and Songjiang Complete

Railway Construction Workers Strike!
Chinese workers, complaining of inadequate pay and difficult working conditions, have refused to return to work in a carefully coordinated strike. Despite the presence of railway unions in the Northeast, their coordination in this instance suggests the involvement of the Communications Clique, possibly as part of an attempt to demonstrate their influence or retaliate for some perceived slight.\n\nWhile this turn of events effects them too, the Japanese are happy to watch us squabble amongst ourselves. The strike will end, but not without causing significant delays.
Unfortunate.
Delays Plague Infrastructure Construction
The nature of the situation was fairly clear as soon as the first signs appeared; shipments unaccountably missing, rails laid at just enough of an incorrect angle to require complete re-construction, and sudden inspections of the labour force by Japanese agents supposedly seeking 'dangerous criminals'; inspections which inevitably required the suspension of work.\n\nThese same tactics were employed by the Japanese during the 1920s against the Fengtian Clique's railway projects, attempting to slow and discredit Chinese construction in order to limit competition to Mantetsu, and now they seem to be delaying our efforts once again. Unfortunately, there is little we can do.
Frustrating.
Delays Plague Mantetsu Infrastructure Construction
Despite Mantetsu's excellent engineers and equipment, the current railway construction project has encountered repeated delays as workers unaccountably go missing, materials vanish in the night, and bandits raid the camps alongside the rails, only to disappear before Japanese troops arrive.\n\nThe local police and our intelligence services are unwilling to do much to investigate or solve these repeated incidents, instead preferring to watch the Japanese squirm. The fact that Mantetsu received the contract to build the railway is well known to the public, and some patriotic citizens appear to have taken matters into their own hands.
What a pity.
Imperial Fury
Infuriated, the Japanese government today issued a statement declaring an end to various Fengtian aid programmes, including sectors such as research, industrial development, agricultural development, and military armament. The aid should return in some time, as the Japanese cannot afford to let us grow too weak, but until then many functions of our state are crippled.

Japanese Aid Returns

Feng Yong Criticises Japan
Citing the recent expansion of the Japanese military garrison in Shenyang, Feng Yong launched a scathing criticism of Japan and its foreign policy from the Assembly floor. Though other politicians have been known to disparage the Japanese in the past, the premier post within Marshal Zhang's cirle gives Feng's words a different kind of significance, and elevates them above the confines of the Assembly.\n\nWasting no time, the Japanese Consul-General has already demanded that we remove Feng Yong from office.
Oh dear.
Japan is our fraternal ally...
Mantetsu Protests Railway Construction
Mantetsu's president, Matsuoka Yōsuke, has notified the government of his discovery of our recently resumed railway construction. Frustrated with our attempts to circumvent his company's stranglehold on logistics, Matsuoka has arbitrarily raised the prices on the imported high quality steel we need to complete the project. Steelworks in Japan have proven no more cooperative, likely having already received direction from the Japanese government. Though we could source the material elsewhere, the costs would make the entire project impractical.\n\nAccepting the raised prices would come at a significant political cost, and reduce the number of workers we can hire, but there could be another solution. By claiming to end the project, we could continue to access the steel at normal prices, while secretly continuing construction. By leading Mantetsu employees in circles with extensive red tape, bureaucratic obstructionism, and bogus paperwork, we could likely finish construction before anyone realises. We've done it before. Unfortunately, due to the secrecy of the project, it'd likely take much longer.
Prices are prices.
They won't notice until it's too late.
The Kwantung Army Tears up our new Railway
Apparently having discovered our deception, soldiers from the Kwantung Army's 'Railway Guard' stormed our ongoing railway construction project, savagely destroying the rails and leaving dozens of dead workers; shot for supposed 'hostile interference'. Though the Japanese were unable to destroy everything, large sections of rail were even melted and twisted into 'railway ties'. To add to the challenges facing resumption of the project, prices on Japanese steel have been raised sky-high, likely at Mantetsu's behest. Though the Japanese are unable to completely stop our work, now we need to start almost from square one.
These insufferable Japanese!
[FNG.GetLeader] is Building Parallel Railways!
Word has come to us by way of Mantetsu's intelligence division that [FNG.GetLeader] has resumed one of his old projects, aiming to circumvent our monopoly on Manchuria's rail network. By building parallel railway lines to the SMR and CER, should a war break out between us, Zhang will be able to ferry his men across the region without immediate interference by the Kwantung Army; not to mention without their immediate knowledge. This represents a threat to our interests, and would normally deserve a swift response.\n\nAlready the Kwantung Army is demanding that these insolent Chinese not be allowed to get away with this brazen insult to the nation.
A swift response they shall have!
We have bigger problems.
Japan Ignores Railway Construction
Surprisingly, the Japanese seem to have chosen to ignore our railway construction, despite their discovery of its continuation. Apart from a 'strongly worded letter', lacking any real teeth, the swift and severe response we've come to expect never came. It's possible they see their complete stranglehold on Manchurian transportation as no longer tenable, but more likely they have greater concerns at the moment.
We've run circles around these fools!
Zhang Zongxiang Negotiates New Trade terms
The [QIE.GetAdjective]-German embargo on goods moving to and from the Northeast hit our economy hard. Continued trade was instead routed through the Legation Cities, open as they were to all nations. Although we were able to side-step the embargo, the use of Tianjin and Shanghai as intermediaries came at the cost of additional tariffs, and reliance on third parties. With these businesses, both legitimate and illegitimate, fully aware of their control over an entire region's trade, trade deals have always been lacklustre despite their necessity.\n\nSomehow Zhang Zongxiang has managed to push through years of negotiations however, and secured a deal offering better terms for trade. Rumours swirl that a number of palms were greased in the process, but nobody seems to want to ask questions.
Excellent!
Mantetsu Lifts Railway Restrictions
After some consideration, and in spite of our sometimes fraught relations, Mantetsu's governing board has decided to set aside the restrictions usually placed on our strategic movement. This is undoubtedly an accommodation made in consideration of our newly entered war. Mantetsu will likely reimpose the restrictions when peace is made.
Finally!
Mantetsu Reimposes Railway Restrictions
Given the end of our recently concluded war, Mantetsu's governing board has decided to reimpose its restrictions on our strategic movement in Manchuria.
Naturally...
A New Automobile Company
Thanks to the Shenyang Arsenal's regular production of the Minsheng Truck and our efforts to encourage sino-japanese cooperation, a group of Communications Clique oligarchs have partnered with the Jidōsha-Seizo Company, subsidiary to the Nihon Sangyō Zaibatsu, to fund the creation of a new automobile factory in Fengtian province. Already a collection of young engineers, mostly educated in Japan, are studying the prospects of more modern consumer-oriented Minsheng-inspired models.
Good news!
Japanese involvement is unacceptable.
An End to the Investment Shortage
After roughly a decade of limited external or internal investment beyond the government's own, Fengtian has made itself a reliable and trustworthy location for prosperous growth. Going from strength to strength, and with the fires of industry behind us, our prospects of retaking the country are growing by the day.\n\nAs we begin other development projects, we should begin to see our investment efforts open up related opportunities.
Finally!
Red Spears in Dezhou!
Bands of Red Spears, peasant self-defence units which are often little better than bandits, have grown in size and strength across Dezhou recently, especially along the Zhili-Shandong border. As the new rulers in the area, we are expected to maintain peace and order, which has now been substantially disturbed. Several local garrisons have been attacked, villages burned, and towns raided. Forces have already been dispatched to deal with the issue, but a concerted effort to wipe out resistance in the rear areas, behind our front lines, is likely needed to deal with them permanently.
Damn peasants!
Deserters Rise up in Daming!
When our troops swept through Zhili province, they crushed all signs of organised resistance, but sometimes resistance isn't so organised. Groups of deserters, stemming from our enemy's former armies and our own forces, have begun organising in order to take on larger targets across Daming. Several trains in the vicinity of Shimen have come under attack, and have caused our logisticians serious concern due to the Jinhan Line's major strategic importance. Local garrisons will be mobilised to deal with the issue, but matters such as these behind our lines deserve a coordinated response.
Traitors the lot of them!
Warlords Resist in Ruyang
Composed as they are of informal patronage networks, not all local power structures can be co-opted by our occupying forces. In this case, several local warlords formerly loyal to Wu Peifu have seemingly taken offence at our policies in Ruyang, and seized the Gongxian Arsenal at Xinyang. Despite their relative organisation and the weapons from the arsenal, their troops are still too few and too ill-equipped to combat our own on a large scale, but they will nonetheless force us to divert forces away from the front lines. We need a coherent response to these cases of resistance.
Fools.
Bandits Sweep Guanzhong
The mountains around Xi'an have been home to bandits since time immemorial, but now these brigands have come down from the hills and begun preying on hapless travellers, undefended villages, and most importantly our supply caravans. Due to their diffuse and disorganised nature, bandits can be difficult to track down and eliminate permanently. To do so we will undoubtedly need a coordinated effort.
Well what are we waiting for?
The Soy Agricultural Initiative
Soybeans are an extremely flexible crop, useful for human food, animal feed, fertiliser, and for a wide variety of industrial applications. Mantetsu's Research Wing has made great strides in making their growing, processing, and use more efficient, but planting percentages across Fengtian remain relatively stagnant. Korean farmers, who make up the majority of immigrants to Manchuria, are excellent rice planters, and like many Chinese prefer crops they have more experience with.\n\nIn an attempt to change this, Mantetsu began the Soy Agricultural Initiative, a plan intending to educate farmers and incentivise the production of soy as a cash crop, but it has so far been poorly received. Mantetsu hopes to gain the government's support in promoting the initiative, which would almost certainly increase soy yields and therefore long term profits.\n\nA few dissenting voices have pointed out that excessive soy production could reduce food security in the northeast, and in the right conditions might lead to a famine.
Back the Initiative.
We need no more soy.
Japan and Korea Struggle with Drought
Both Japan and Korea are experiencing severe drought conditions, which we have fortunately been spared, but their economies and people now suffer, and some live on the brink of starvation. The Japanese government has formally demanded that we take part in a programme wherein we provide rice and millet to Korea, which in turn will provide rice to Japan. However, this plan is somewhat confounded by the overwhelming success of Mantetsu's Soy Agricultural Initiative, which replaced vast tracts of rice plots with soy farming. As a result, we have nowhere near enough rice and millet to feed Korea, while our soy production remains key to our industry and international trade.\n\nThanks to Japan's political and economic influence, we have little choice but to comply.
Both Japan and Korea are experiencing severe drought conditions, which we have fortunately been spared, but their economies and people now suffer, and some live on the brink of starvation. The Japanese government has informally asked that we take part in a programme wherein we provide rice and millet to Korea, which in turn will provide rice to Japan. However, this plan is somewhat confounded by the overwhelming success of Mantetsu's Soy Agricultural Initiative, which replaced vast tracts of rice plots with soy farming. As a result, we have nowhere near enough rice and millet to feed Korea, while our soy production remains key to our industry and international trade.\n\nThis is a surprising turn for the typically aloof Japanese, but all the same, while we may refuse, it would almost certainly be met with severe repercussions.

The Industrial Soy Proposal
Our increased food exportation, in order to counter-act the drought currently facing the Home Islands and Korea, has resulted in low provisions across Fengtian and considerable public upset. Some government ministers have proposed cutting production of industrial soy, thus providing sufficient food but handicapping our civilian industry and some exports until the crisis is resolved.
Cut industrial soy production.

The Drought Ends
After months of hardship, the drought in Korea and Japan has ended. We are no longer expected to render any aid to Japan or Korea.
Finally!
A Proposal from Mantetsu
A representative from Mantetsu's Research Wing has come forward with a proposal, the acceptance of which he assures us is in our best interest, but which he insists must be kept completely secret. Apparently, following the Drought of 1939, Mantetsu brought together farming experts, senior officials from agricultural organisations, and academic scholars with the aim of improving agricultural efficiency and production in the Northeast. After months of testing, one of several research teams created a solution based upon farming methods used in Hokkaido, which might allow the average Chinese family to farm ten entire hectares of land without needing to hire seasonal workers, thus improving production and freeing up labour for factories in Anshan, Fushun, and Shenyang. The Mantetsu official indicates that these methods should be spread through the dissemination of informational leaflets and Chinese instructors, themselves trained by Japanese experts, and he seemed to stress the idea that this project should be disassociated in every possible way from the South Manchurian Railway.\n\nAfter some investigation, the Army's intelligence section has determined that the Kwantung Army refused to support Mantetsu's efforts, suggesting that the two factions may be competing, or that this is simply a part of some elaborate Japanese ruse. The relatively liberal officials in Mantetsu's research wing and other bureaucratic offices have been known to clash with the conservative Kwantung Army.
Accept the proposal.
Refuse the proposal.
Hokkaido Farming Bears Fruit
After much time and effort, the Hokkaido farming methods proposed by Mantetsu seem to be bearing fruit in some areas, increasing production, and freeing up additional land in the north.
Excellent.
Discovery
Although no public announcement has been made, Mantetsu's research wing has communicated that the Kwantung Army discovered our collaborative farming effort, a claim backed up by findings from our intelligence services. General Ueda Kenkichi himself is said to have stormed into the office of the Mantetsu president, Matsuoka Yōsuke, and delivered a thunderous verbal barrage regarding the necessity of Fengtian's continued state of dependence. The Kwantung Army's ability to punish Mantetsu is ultimately limited, as the powerful company is practically autonomous, but there's little doubt that the Army will go out of its way to make things difficult for everyone involved. Unfortunately, this will certainly be the end of this specific collaboration project with Mantetsu.
Unfortunate.
Discovery
Although no public statement has been made, the recent signs of discontent within portions of the army leadership have become difficult to ignore. Apparently word of our farming collaboration project with Mantetsu has spread further than we anticipated, and according to some nationalistically inclined generals, 'China must reform itself' and not submit to 'forced restructuring disguised as collaborative reform'.\n\nAlthough this is far from a major crisis, any threat to the continued cooperation of our generals and other officials is no laughing matter. Some ministers suggest that we might defend our collaboration, painting it as an instance in which we are able to manipulate Mantetsu, instead of the other way around. Others suggest that this may simply dig our hole deeper.
Guilty as charged.

Popular Opinion Shifts in Our Favour
Against what seemed to be all odds, Grand Marshal Zhang's defence of the Hokkaido farming project seems to have convinced all those concerned. The impact has been mitigated, and the programme can continue uninterrupted.
Wonderful news!
The Public is Incensed!
Despite our bureaucrat's best efforts, and even those of Grand Marshal Zhang, many prominent figures in the military remain unconvinced that the Hokkaido Farming Project is worth our while. As a result, the programme will almost certainly grind to a halt, and our divided government faces yet another point of contention.

Enrich the Country, Strengthen the Army
After decades of decline and destitution, the necessity of progress and development has never been more glaring. However, while we cannot afford to stagnate, change comes with its own risks - namely mismanagement and public discontent.\n\nThe task falls to the government to answer calls to 'Enrich the Country and Strengthen the Army', but we must prioritise one or the other.
We must enrich the Country!

Tell me more about the state of the Economy.
Tell me more about the state of the Army.
Enrich the Country
While Manchuria's resources are rich and diverse, and Fengtian stands as the third greatest industrial centre in East Asia, its economy remains plagued by a number of structural problems, the symptoms of which cripple the state and slow progress toward Southern Reclamation. Fengtian's biggest investor is the state itself, feeding tax revenues back into key sectors such as steel, coal, and soybean production. Yet, the Japanese and Mantetsu trail the government only marginally in this regard, and invest far more widely, giving them an unquestioned grip upon both Fengtian's economy and society.\n\nWhile the extent of this grip grows by the day, reform could serve to increase the government's revenues through the suppression of otherwise endemic corruption, the creation of a healthier environment for private investment, and the unfortunate but necessary cooperation with Mantetsu in key areas like infrastructure and technology. So long as the government can maintain political autonomy, and at least a majority of control over the economy, it can pursue initiatives to contest Japanese influence, retain legitimacy in the eyes of the Chinese people, and eventually achieve its core goals.\n\nIt should be noted that while Japan has a vested interest in seeing us succeed relative to [QIE.GetNameDef], they will only provide assistance with specific efforts aiming to move past our backward industry, even as they attempt to widen their already worrying influence over our economy.
Let us enrich the country!
Perhaps the Army is more important?
Strengthen the Army
The Fengtian Army, officially the Army of the Republic, is an impressive sight by most Chinese standards, though pales in comparison to most foreign forces, and has only recently recovered much of its strength after its decimation in the last Zhifeng War. The majority of Fengtian's weapons and vehicles are outdated, even including its standard issue rifle provided by the Japanese, and organisation below the division level is a patchy affair due to limited communications equipment. The Army's greatest deficiency is in morale, partially as a consequence of foreign-trained and even outright Japanese officers widespread throughout the ranks.\n\nMeanwhile, the Fengtian Flying Corps, officially The China Flying Corps, is the pride and joy of the Grand Marshal's oldest son, Zhang Xueliang, who used his passion for aviation to train its first pilots. The Flying Corps performed well during the war, and lost air superiority over the Zhili only upon the arrival of modern German-piloted planes. Since then, the Corps has grown slightly, though its planes remain over a decade behind the European standard.\n\nOverall, Fengtian's forces lag behind those of [QIE.GetNameDef], and remain heavily dependent upon Japanese equipment and aid. This aid, and whatever Fengtian can do to become self-sufficient, will be crucial to narrowing that gap and eventually reclaiming the south.
Let us strengthen the Army!
But what of the economy?
An Empty-Handed Return
Despite their best efforts, the scientists and engineers we dispatched to study Japanese manufacturing methods have returned empty-handed. Perhaps the sheer disparity in sophistication between their technology and our own was a hindrance, or maybe the Japanese went out of their way to be unhelpful. Whatever the case, the general population seems to have been impressed more by the apparent accomplishment of our 'top men' than their failure, as this has gone mysteriously unreported. As far as anyone knows, our scientists went overseas to receive very prestigious awards.
Top men.
Yamato Hotel Licences
Mantetsu's Yamato Hotel line has long been a staple of the South Manchuria Railway Zone; the concessions zone ceded first to Imperial Russia and then to Japan after 1906, and then expanded following the 21 demands of 1915 through a rather loose interpretation of its provisions to include all of southern Manchuria. All the same, while treaty rights permit Japanese to reside and engage in business and manufacture of any kind, construction still theoretically requires approval from the local governor and, if necessary, the Grand Marshal himself.\n\nMantetsu aims to build a series of new hotels, all of which will inevitably become hubs for further Japanese activity, and while construction could never be stopped without angering the Japanese government, limits might be imposed to forestall Japanese influence in certain areas. Unfortunately, as much as they may stand as physical edifices of Japan's strength, the hotels are frequented by the Japanese elite and many Mantetsu employees, making them crucial for the rapid development we desire.
Limit construction.
Let them build as they please.
The Northeast Industrial Development Commission
At Japan's request, and with no particular reason to refuse, we have established a legal and fiscal framework enabling the creation of the Northeast Industrial Development Commission. Serving to oversee and direct the development of Fengtian's industry, mostly through the allocation of funds and leases, the commission now faces the question of its composition.\n\nThe Concordia Association has proposed the inclusion of a series of extremely talented individuals with experience working for the Nissan and Mitsubishi Zaibatsu in Japan, who stress the need for an export-driven economy taking advantage of Fengtian's existing natural resources, while the Grand Marshal's generals insist upon the necessity of an 'Army First' approach to development, and are using their considerable influence to ensure the placement of military men on the commission. The Communications Clique recommends their own presence, and advocate a mixed developmental approach, referencing their long experience with business dealings across China, as well as more recently here in the Northeast.\n\nUnfortunately, a compromise involving all three parties is practically impossible, as a clear vision is necessary for the task, and intra-commission bickering would almost certainly render it functionally impotent. Additionally, although the commission's nature as an appointed body permits the presence of Japanese in its makeup, the public and much of the Assembly will likely react negatively to their presence. At the same time, the Japanese will not appreciate exclusion.

Mantetsu Chōsabu
The South Manchuria Railway Company's Research Wing, colloquially known as 'Mantetsu Chōsabu', has grown over the years from a mere corporate R&D department into the heart of Japan's colonial research programme, with divisions dedicated to everything from agricultural science to intelligence gathering. The organisation's sheer scale has lead to the opening of offices in Berlin, Vancouver, and New York to attract foreign talent, plus wide recruitment from Japan's foremost universities. The result is a surprisingly liberal and open-minded intellectual community, which sometimes places scientific inquiry before nationalistic concerns.\n\nThis appears to be one of those instances, as our government has been approached by a Chōsabu representative offering future assistance in one of several fields. It should be noted that the Kwantung Army garrison in [745.GetCapitalVictoryPointName] were strongly opposed to this arrangement.

The Jinzhou Industrial Zone
Jinzhou's convenient location makes it excellent for a proposed industrial zone, and several groups have already begun jockeying for a dominant position in development; most notably a Mantetsu subsidiary specialising in canning and light metal work, the Communications Clique who want to establish a rolling stock factory, and the military which insists that the zone must be used for munitions manufacture ahead of 'personal capitalistic gains'. The situation is made somewhat unusual by the Communications Clique, who are usually able to front quite a bit of money, and rumours suggest that several members are under pressure from the military to weaken their own bidding position.

Filling the Silver Reserve
A full silver reserve is crucial to building confidence in Fengtian's currency, and even more crucial to attracting foreign investment, without which Fengtian can never hope to match the Zhili to the south who have been, for the past eight years, flush with German capital. However, silver is an expensive commodity, and paying for enough to fill the reserve fully would undoubtedly cut funding from other areas.\n\nSome ministers have privately suggested only buying about half of the desired quantity, as many believed the reserve was less than full before the last Zhifeng War, and those rumours were never confirmed. Of course, it was later difficult to explain the significant economic recession that followed the government's inability to settle its war debts.\n\nStill, filling the reserve inadequately would certainly be a big risk, but perhaps a worthwhile one.

Economic Disaster!
After the Bank of Japan and Mitsui Bank, major lenders to our own government, unexpectedly called for outstanding debts to be paid, our Central Bank suddenly found itself unable to provide sufficient silver for the transaction. News of the situation quickly leaked to the public provoking a run on the banks, and widespread financial panic. Rumour suggests that the crisis is not a product of gross mismanagement and incompetence on behalf of the government, which would surprise few in Fengtian, but rather a deliberate move to deceive the public. Mantetsu's offices in Shenyang and Harbin have already begun a full scale investigation, and unless action is taken they seem likely to discover a very incriminating paper trail.\n\nWhile there are several options available, it would be unfortunate if certain government files inexplicably went missing...

The State of the Officer Corps
Fengtian's officer corps is an unusual mix of young Chinese educated at either the Rikugun Shikan Gakkō in Japan, the Northeastern Army Lecture Hall, or the Baoding Military Academy, older Chinese who served in the Civil Wars, and Japanese officers part of the Military Mission to Fengtian, all united by common loyalties to individuals more than any special dedication to the state. Japanese officers in particular are known to prize any station in the Northeast, the devalued currency allowing them to live lives of relative luxury, and hire servants for most menial tasks, earning them the enmity of not only their fellows but also the local population.\n\nNow, with the founding of the Shenyang National Academy, these officers have taken the opportunity to mock the academy's current accommodations, which are decades old and in disrepair. The Anshan Incident
As Anshan's ore lies close to the surface, its mines have mainly expanded outward rather than downward, swallowing up nearby land at an alarming pace. Our decision to approve the company's further expansion has thus led to the complete destruction of several nearby farmsteads, and half a village, at the hands of Japanese mining equipment.\n\nPromised compensation has not been forthcoming, and protests quickly broke out among local farmers, which our local police refused to break up on 'patriotic grounds'. The ensuing riot severely damaged expensive mining equipment, leading to the deployment of the Japanese railway guard, and the use of lethal force to disperse the riot. This slaughter of our citizens has not gone unnoticed, and existing anti-Japanese sentiment has only been inflamed. The people will hold us accountable in our response, but the deposits and the company working them are essential to Japan's strategic goals, and our relationship with the Japanese permits little room to manoeuvre.

The Five Colours
The Jilin Film Association has today released its first feature, a sweeping ethnographic detailing the diverse populations of the Northeast, from the snow-capped pines of Heilongjiang to the fertile banks of the lower Liao River, espousing the values of the national 'Five Races under One Union' policy.\n\nThanks to government assistance, the Association was able to easily access a number of remote locations in order to film and better spread its message of unity and harmony, though some criticism has been levelled at its coverage of Koreans and Japanese, many of whom also cohabit the Northeast, but are not officially a part of the 'Five Races' designated in the national flag. Overall, and despite its relatively small screening due to limited theatre numbers, the film has been considered a great success.

Aside from some first-time viewers being scared out of the theatre, the overall message is demeaning, playing to Japanese assumptions that Chinese are, by habit, dirty and lice-infested; the reception being quite negative as a result, and leading some to wonder whether this might have been avoided if the government took a more active role in production.

Honghuzi Crushed!
After an extensive hunt, the Honghuzi were tracked to the foot of a mountain referred to by the locals as 'Hushan', or 'Tiger Mountain'. The bandits fought to the death, resisting an assault by several thousand regulars for nearly three hours; steep inclines, narrow paths, and hidden caverns aiding their defence.\n\nA number of prisoners from the surrounding villages were liberated, alongside a significant sum in valuables. The camp was then set alight, creating a spectacle visible for miles around.

With the Heilongjiang Clique's miniature Insurgency in full swing, the government and provincial authorities in the region, alongside Japanese aid, have engaged in a fierce crackdown campaign against the wannabe vigilantes and heros. Whilst resembling the various bandit groups that have roamed the Three Northeastern Provinces for years, the Heilongjiang Insurgency took on the form of a far more organised, and capable, force. Even with noted blunders under the command of Wu Junsheng and Wan Fulin, the desperados continuously managed to trump Fengtian forces.\n\nOr so was the case up until recently. Chasing up the ladder of provincial insurgent HQs, and through systematic deployment of Kempetai interrogation and bribery of less than convicted cadres of the rebel's escapades, Ma Zhanshan, Wan Fulin, and Wu Junsheng fell akin to dominoes. First to fall was Wan Fulin, proving to be little more capable than his days in the broader Fengtian army. Then came Wu Junsheng, unable to stem the tide, perishing ironically due to a local explosive carried by a double agent. Third arrived Zhang Tingshu, collaborating with the Kuomintang insurgents, he would ultimately suffer the fate of many of China's prior revolutionaries.\n\nFinally arrived Ma Zhanshan, proving to be the most resilient of the three. An expert at maintaining the primacy, mobility, and cohesiveness of his broadly cavalry force, Ma defiantly resisted to the brutal and bitter end. For the first time, Mantetsu's 'Asia Express' streamlined train will be running from the tip of [745.GetCapitalVictoryPointName] to the northern city of Harbin, at an astonishing 130 kilometres an hour, putting it among the fastest trains in the world. Evidence has come to the Grand Marshal's attention suggesting that vast sums of development money were funnelled into Mantetsu sponsored schools and hospitals, each of which used the sudden boost in funding to further its efforts in promoting Sino-Japanese friendship. No doubt other members of his party are complicit, and while some measure of corruption is of little surprise to the public, a scandal on this scale will upset even the highest ranks of government.
Who can be trusted anymore?

General Tang Yulin has been spotted audaciously seated atop a ravenous tiger somewhere in Rehe Province! The CER Tax Dispute
The levying of seemingly arbitrary taxes to fill gaps in the budget, genuine or not, has been a long standing practice of national, regional, and local governments across China, including our own. This time, Police Chief Yuan is pressuring the Director of the Chinese Eastern Railway, Li Shaogeng, to accept additional taxes on the railway, allegedly for the purposes of further strengthening the army. If his demands aren't met, he's threatening an investigation of Communications Clique assets, as well as various legally questionable fees the Board already charges its customers, the revenue from which almost certainly sticks to a number of fingers.\n\nThere is every likelihood that, as Yuan is likewise a member of the CER board and an advisor on our inner council, this is his idea of a power play. Still, it must be said, his tax would undoubtedly help fill the national treasury, if at the cost of undercutting competition to Mantetsu. It seems likely that the Grand Marshal will be forced to settle this dispute, lest it spiral out of control.

Reclaiming the Jinhan Railway
Reclaiming the Jinpu Railway
Reclaiming the Yuehan Railway
Originally financed by Belgian capital, the Jinghan Railway runs north-to-south from Beijing in Zhili to Hankou in Hubei. For decades it has served as one of China's primary transit arteries, ferrying goods across the length of the North China Plain, and connecting its width by way of Zhengzhou.\n\nIn the years since its construction the railway has fallen on hard times, and so while the Belgians are long gone it will take a great deal of investment to restore its infrastructure and integrate it with our new national railway services.

Financed by British and German capital nearly fifteen years before the Weltkrieg, the Jinpu Railway runs north-to-south from Tianjin to Pukou, a district of Nanjing. Like the Jinghan Railway, it has long served as one of China's most important logistical arteries, connecting north with south, and east with west by way of Xuzhou.\n\nIn the years since the last Zhifeng War the sections of the railway in Shandong and Jiangsu gradually fell under the sway of the German AOG, which updated and expanded its infrastructure. However, as the company's employees have now been driven away or shot as Hanjian they will need to be replaced. Unfortunately the process of finding and paying these individuals, not to mention re-integrating the railway itself, could prove a costly enterprise.
$fengtian_events.193.d.jinpu$ $ask_Mantetsu_for_railway$
The Yuehan Railway, connecting Hankou and Guangdong, was born amid a conflict between Belgian and American investors, and as such took abnormally long to complete once both parties pulled out of the project. The railway was ultimately completed under the supervision of the German AOG in the early 1930s, and remained under their control until the collapse of Sun Chuanfang's League.\n\nWith the Germans gone it will need entirely new management and integration into the new national railway system. This will be an expensive task.

The Mantetsu Rail System
With Mantetsu's staff taking up residence in the latest 'reclaimed' railway headquarters, the company has decided to establish two regional subsidiaries to supervise activities in North and Central China. The North China Transportation Company, headquartered in Beijing, will take control of operations between Shanhaiguan and the Yangtze, while the Central China Transportation Company will operate between there and Guangzhou in the south. Ironically, the Japanese have now achieved what the German AOG never could.
A marvel of engineering.

A Compromise Solution
It is clear that Chen will not relent unless he can at least call himself master of Jiangsu (Xuzhou, Yancheng, Nantong states) in some way. Zhang will also never be happy with being stuck with only Shandong. This means that we will have to split Jiangsu, one way or another. One possibility is to simply split the western Xuzhou region, which would go to Zhang, from the eastern Yancheng region, with the latter including Nantong and going to Chen. It is unlikely Chen will see this as sufficient as the province was ruled from Xuzhou, which is also where the province's most important railroads meet. Another possibility is to separate economic from political control. In this scenario, one would officially run Jiangsu's government, which would of course have to be led by at least a somewhat independent governor. Then the other would be allowed to nominate a lieutenant governor, who would have control over all the province's resources and be allowed to levy taxes and conduct recruitment among other things.
Split Jiangsu between them.
Chen gets Jiangsu, exploitation rights to Zhang.
Zhang gets Jiangsu, exploitation rights to Chen.

The Matter of Occupation
Occupations are never easy or simple, but the average Chinese soldier is often little better than a bandit with marching orders. Already our troops have begun burning, looting, and defiling the same towns and villages that our government claims to be liberating. Some would say that we should let the troops have their fun, but now that Grand Marshal Zhang Zuolin is again competing on the national stage he must consider his image. He was once a bandit himself, and many here in the south have a hard time showing respect to or taking orders from a former criminal. Already the elite have turned up their noses, and while force might be an easy answer, we do need these intellectuals, landlords, and businessmen to forward our greater aims. It is these figures through whom we must rule. Fortunately, our logistics system is sufficient to feed our soldiers, meaning our men are not looting for survival, but nonetheless they will be unhappy to be kept from what they see as their right by conquest.\n\nHere we must choose: The liberators or the liberated?

As we extend our authority over newly reclaimed areas, we must ensure that they too do their part in the march toward reunification. Scandal in Beijing
A certain amount of looting was inevitable in Beijing. As the national capital for centuries, and home to generations of emperors, the wealth spread throughout the city's rampant bureaucracy has long been beyond measure. However, it is not material wealth that has seen the city now dragged into scandal. Supposedly some of our soldiers have been capturing the wives and concubines of government ministers and, after committing unspeakable acts, parading them through the city streets as trophies. To make matters worse, some have been placed on a makeshift scaffold and are being sold as if cattle to the highest bidder. In any disciplined army they would be executed for this behaviour, and we have made assurances as such to the local population, but there is every possibility that the matter will be brushed under the rug by local commanders.

Desecration in Yi County
Alarming news has emerged from Yi County in Zhili Province, where a number of Fengtian Army soldiers have blown open the entrance to several of the Western Qing Tombs. Ever since the vulgar desecration of Dowager Empress Cixi's resting place in 1928, by Zhang's indirect subordinate Sun Dianying no less, this subject has been used to damage the Grand Marshal's reputation in certain circles. With this new episode, so similar to the last, there may be no true recovery. The exact amount of wealth stolen from the tombs is unclear, but the soldiers involved disappeared into the reeds along Lake Baiyangdian, and the majority will likely make its way onto the black market soon.
