Disorder at Baoding
Disturbing reports have begun to emerge from Baoding Military Academy, which a company of our soldiers recently captured and occupied. As a military target in which the enemy held out for over a week, damage to the building was expected, as was some degree of looting, but few expected to hear of our men killing one another over the spoils. Supposedly the institution's store of medals and rank insignia was discovered shortly after its capture, creating several self-declared colonels, majors, and generals, each belonging to a variety of self-awarded honourable orders. These men, completely ignorant of the actual standing granted by their regalia, began to fight over precedence. By the time troops arrived from elsewhere to relieve the actual commander, the upstart soldiers had split into a number of cliques occupying different parts of the academy, and several dozen were dead.
There can only be one Grand Marshal.
Order Returns to Zhili Province
After a wave of spontaneous and occasionally indiscriminate looting, burning, and other criminal behaviour by our troops, order has returned to Zhili Province. By and large, the soldiers simply burned themselves out. This episode will not be regarded highly by the peasants who bore the brunt of the violence, nor by landlords, business owners, or government officials. While this will eventually blur together with the rest of the atrocities of the warlord era, it will make governing the vast areas of newly conquered territory no easier.
After our troops swept across Zhili Province the majority of the population braced themselves for a wave of indiscriminate violence. But, despite a few unavoidable incidents, our troops have largely kept to the code of conduct set out by Marshal Zhang. Some stubborn figures have attributed the surprise to Fengtian's advanced system of logistics, which reduced the need for our armies to live off of the land, instead of praising Zhang himself. Still, even they cannot ignore results, and this performance will go a long way toward earning the nation's trust.
At least it's over.
Railway Chaos in Zhengzhou
Apparently, as soon as our troops seized Zhengzhou, they descended on its railway station. As the heart of the nation's railway network in wartime, and perhaps due our enemies' dogged attempts to defend it, the tracks were crowded with rolling stock - full to the brim with refugee belongings and war materiel. The subsequent orgy of looting has seen railway traffic in the area backed up for days, as every last car has been ransacked, and while we have seized a certain amount of military equipment from the cars, the majority are now wrecked and unusable. It will take a long time to clear them from the railway, and longer still for the city's former residents to forget the blatant theft of their belongings.
Apparently, as soon as our troops seized Zhengzhou, they descended on its railway station. As the heart of the nation's railway network in wartime, and perhaps due our enemies' dogged attempts to defend it, the tracks were crowded with rolling stock - full to the brim with refugee belongings and war materiel. Looting began almost immediately, but fortunately some of our officers were able to limit the activity to only half of the rail cars, with the officers themselves taking only a further quarter. Consequently what might have turned into a logistical disaster, where looted rolling stock blocked the tracks for days, became a relatively orderly affair that left at least something behind for the city's residents.
What's left?
Bandits against Bandits
Our troops recently seized Luoyang alongside most of Henan Province's major cities, but securing the countryside has proven another matter. Banditry has long history in Henan, and despite nearly a decade of Zhili rule this problem never truly went away. The majority were simply incorporated into Wu Peifu's armies. Now they are sweeping across the province's rural regions, and having 'defected' to our side, are claiming the spoils of a war they never won.\n\nOur own troops, feeling cheated, are now engaging in competitive looting and destruction, occasionally escalating into localised but coordinated battles. The planned arrival of some more orderly troops to the area ought to calm tensions so that the actual bandits can be rounded up, but the damage is already done. The combined destruction is being compared to a natural disaster.

Banditry has long history in Henan, and despite nearly a decade of Zhili rule this problem never truly went away. The majority were simply incorporated into Wu Peifu's armies. Now they are sweeping across the province's rural regions, and having 'defected' to our side, have begun claiming the spoils of a war they never won.\n\nOur own troops have stepped in to quell the violence, but thoroughly combing Henan's hills and riversides will take time and energy; neither of which our troops would prefer to spend. In all likelihood bandit activity will resume again some time in the future, and everything already stolen is now in the hands of our own troops.
Bandits everywhere!
Order Returns to Henan Province
After transportation chaos, endemic violence, and a wave of all too familiar banditry, Henan province has settled back into relative normality. Times are still hard for the average peasant, and brigands still roam the hills, but by and large our own troops have burned themselves out and settled down. Henan in particular has seen its fair share of famine, violence, and other tragedy, in which this may be little more than a historical footnote, but for the lives it touched, and certainly the lives it claimed, the events of [GetYear] will never be forgotten.
After some inevitable violence, and a wave of all too familiar banditry, Henan has settled back into relative normality. The province is no stranger to tragedy, and so the relatively decent conduct of our troops throughout has turned some heads. Local business owners, landlords, and government officials appreciate our soldiers' restraint, and it's their support that will be essential to governing the province in the future.
At least it's over.

Victory in Wuhan
China's republican dream was born in Wuhan, and today we are its torchbearers. Sadly revolutionary ideals were far from the minds of our soldiers who, after encountering unexpected resistance in Wuchang, proceeded to run wild through the city, looting indiscriminately. By the time order was restored, the docks, wharfs, and all manner of river-side businesses were reduced to ashes, along with sizeable residential areas. What might have otherwise served as political victory became a political defeat, and a mark of shame.\n\nOn a more positive note, our troops were able to recover a stockpile of equipment from the now abandoned Hanyang Arsenal, though it is suspected that a certain number of weapons were siphoned away and onto the black market.
China's republican dream was born in Wuhan, and today we are its torchbearers. Disaster at the Daye Mines
Ore has been mined at Daye for over two thousand years, and today iron from its depths feeds the fires of modern industry in Wuhan, Hubei, and the Lower Yangtze. This did nothing to stop our soldiers, who upon hearing rumours that gold was to be found there, plundered the mine and, in their disappointment at finding nothing of the sort, collapsed its entrance - trapping over one hundred miners inside. A rescue effort has been proposed, but such expense is widely considered wasted on common labourers. Those responsible for the disaster, meanwhile, have deserted and are nowhere to be found.

Miners Rescued in Daye
By the time our men broke through to the trapped miners in Daye, all had perished. While this is certainly not the outcome we were hoping for, the fact that our men tried at all has been received well by the local community, and more importantly by national newspapers.
Thanks to an old O&K steam shovel brought over from a neighbouring mine, our soldiers were able to break through in time to rescue dozens of miners. Despite their initial reservations, the men seem to feel that the heartfelt gratitude of the labourers and their families made it well worth the effort, and praise by national newspapers has offset most political fallout from the disaster itself.\n\nTo add to the positive turn of events, an assortment of weapons crates were brought up by the grateful miners, which had apparently been stashed there during the enemy's retreat not so long ago.

Remember the Experience in Ju
The years since the formation of our Government have laid for us a solid foundation for national regeneration. We fear no problems, nor are we concerned over impending dangers. We merely lament the fate of the South, the freedom of which was originally brought about by the hard efforts and sacrifices of reformist patriots, and which has since been erased by the old and outmoded forms of government. Today, her people are powerless, and her rulers without integrity, thus allowing the slow degradation of the national condition, and the return to a state of total subservience to Western nations. These old ways are sapping China's national strength, shaking her national foundations, and subjugating her people.\n\nIt is thus that we find ourselves in the North, as the final bastion of all that our predecessors struggled to build, and the bearers of the future of a new China. The regressive [QIE.GetAdjective] government likes to say that, by fortifying the Northeast, we are 'digging a hole to die in'. To this I say 'Forget not what happened in Ju'. It was to Ju that the State of Qi retreated, and from there that it reconquered all that it had lost. When the time is right, the Northeast will be our Ju, and the whole of China will be our Qi. Our victory is inevitable, long live the Republic!

The Grand Marshal's Proclamation
An old proverb says: 'Virtue never lacks company; it will ever find support.' The forces of justice will rise, and men of goodwill ultimately cooperate in the interests of rectitude. There is little question that the regressive and illegitimate [QIE.GetAdjective] government stands in the way of progress, oppressing and subjugating the Chinese people, and I have received every assurance that our allies will stand with us to end this injustice. On our part, we should hold fast, fix our eyes steadfastly on our goal, and be firm in our determination. The entire Northeast should carry on with oneness of heart. The final victory will be ours. I urge my ministers, our army, and our people to redouble their efforts in order to attain success.\n\nIt is in this spirit, that I proclaim the beginning of the Year of Righteous Effort, a full three hundred and sixty five days of strenuous national effort, from which we shall emerge as a force unstoppable in the pursuit of our goal. And, when this year is done, the Five Colour Flag will fly high again in Beijing, and the [QIE.GetAdjective] government will be nothing but ash in the winds of history. Ten thousand years to the Republic! Zhonghua Mingguo Wansui!

Zhang Zuolin's Gambit
Although Marshal Zhang agreed to sign Tokyo's Treaties of Friendship upon his return to Beijing, Japan always suspected that perhaps he was hoping to renegotiate the concessions after unification was carried out. Tokyo had hoped to keep Marshal Zhang's government paralysed from attempting renegotiation through the Pro-Japanese Front, but it seems that the Old Marshal has mustered enough political momentum within his halls of power to send our ambassador notice of his intent to renegotiate China's continued status within the Co-Prosperity Sphere.\n\nIn exchange for maintaining the current alliance with Tokyo, Zhang wishes for the return of all concessions, the dismantling of extra-territoriality, the withdrawal of Japanese forces in China, and the de facto nationalisation of Mantetsu and other Japanese companies in China. While Japan will continue to enjoy the fruits of its economic investments, its previous privileged status will be greatly undone. Although Marshal Zhang's proposal is full of cordial language, it is clear to Tokyo that refusal will result in the Anguojun Government taking decisive action to secure their interests. Marshal Zhang's offer has infuriated many in the Japanese Government, though others recognise that war with a united China will be a costly endeavour that may not develop to Japan's favour.

In a final act of defiance, the enemy detonated explosives inside several factories, but by daybreak silence ruled the city - broken only by occasional gunshots marking the executions of survivors.\n\nHarbin is ours once again.

Though war with the rest of China is expected, he has staved off challenges to his leadership from within.

Zhang Asks to Join the Sphere
In the Beijing Conference, it became clear that Marshal Zhang's stance towards Tokyo would be the primary topic of discussion. Various minor warlords argued for or against us, as did Zhang's many factions in Shenyang. Of the major factions not directly aligned with us, the Recovery League was mainly divided, the New Communications Clique threw their weight in favour of us despite their recent business disputes with the Concordia Association, the Zhang Clique was mostly against us, and the Shikan Clique was divided, but leaned towards us.\n\nAlongside the debates at the highest levels of government, on the street the Federation of Chinese Democratic Parties organised protests of nationalistic students to rally against continued Japanese influence. With our ambassador directly pressuring him to sign treaties of friendship and formal entry into the Co-Prosperity Sphere, Zhang has finally made his move.\n\nMuch to our approval, Zhang has agreed to join the Co-Prosperity Sphere without any stipulations. Perhaps Zhang hopes to negotiate for greater concessions after unification, where his leverage will be higher, but that will not be an issue for Tokyo. We can prevent Zhang from demanding much of anything if the Fengtian Pro-Japanese front and our agents in China work to maintain our influence in his government.

Our Entry into the Sphere
With our entry into the Co-Prosperity Sphere, we can expect much more significant Japanese aid in the struggle to come. Marshal Zhang's rivals in the South have already denounced him as a traitor to the Chinese nation, and have openly called for a United Front to jointly fight off the Anguojun and Japanese. Marshal Zhang is less concerned about the United Front, instead already looking to his ambitions after unification is carried out. The Old Marshal is already scheming to retake the coastal concessions after unification is carried out against his rivals, and keep Japanese influence at a minimum, as he did a decade ago.

The United Front are unlikely to win this war against the Japanese Goliath, but perhaps they will go down as the last stand of a Free China.

Our Allies in Tokyo
Zhang Zuolin is proud to have survived decades of China's brutal power games, but the reality is he could not have done it alone nor would his dreams of reunifying the country be realistic if it was not for the patronage of Japan. Many of our rivals paint him as a stooge for foreign imperialists, and even more embarrassing a power that China once saw as akin to a younger brother, but the reality is more nuanced.\n\nZhang Zuolin and many other politicians sympathetic to Japan do seek cooperation with Japan and are willing to make pragmatic concessions to advance their interests, but they also often believe that once China is united they will inevitably have the leverage to renegotiate treaties as equals. Their personal motivations also vary - some are cynically hoping to preserve their own power and wealth while others sincerely buy into Japanese Pan-Asian rhetoric against European powers.\n\nWhatever the case, Japan's outsized influence adds another layer of intrigue in Fengtian Clique politics. Japan expects returns on their investments, but conceding too much to Japan has brought down entire governments in the past - a lesson the exile Anhui and Communications Clique have learned the hard way.\n\nJapan's agents on the ground often fight and compete among themselves as they execute competing agendas often without Tokyo's knowledge. Zhang has been willing to exploit the lack of strategic clarity among Japanese decision-makers, but it also means that many of the deals he makes lack permanence for both sides. Managing expectations from both sides will be integral in his quest to liberate his nation.

Still, our efforts at establishing a hegemony over China have been stymied, even after the Xinhai Revolution and the ensuing Warlord Era tore apart the fragile nation. In addition to surges of Chinese nationalism and also the interference of Western powers, a lack of consistent strategic clarity from Tokyo has caused our various forces on the continent to adopt their own rival agendas.\n\nWhile this strategic ambiguity does offer plausible deniability and flexibility, it has hampered the establishment of a cohesive strategy for handling Chinese affairs. Tensions in Manchuria
Ever since the fall of the Anhui Clique, the Fengtian Clique and Zhili Clique have regarded each other as their principal rival. The Zhili first gained the upper hand in the First ZhiFeng war, but Fengtian nearly toppled the entire clique in 1924. However, Zhang Zuolin was ousted yet again in 1927 following Zhili victory against the KMT. For around a decade, Zhang Zuolin has sat north of the Great Wall, licking his wounds and plotting his eventual return to Beijing. It seems that this period of buildup has finally run its course, and Marshal Zhang has embarked on one final campaign to not just seize Beijing, but unify all of China.\n\nAlthough Tokyo has been allied to Marshal Zhang's government for nearly two decades, Japanese policy towards the Fengtian Clique continues to be divided and contradictory. The Tianjin Army has largely been supportive of Zhang's National Reclamation War. They hope that by aiding Marshal Zhang in his war, the Tianjin Army will be able to insert themselves as China's real rulers from behind the scenes, even perhaps eliminating their Kwantung rivals. Conversely, the Kwantung Army has long maintained their influence in Manchuria, and are very concerned of the possibility of Marshal Zhang losing the war, which would result in the loss of their own influence.\n\nEven within the Fengtian Clique, there have been those with concerns regarding the National Reclamation War's feasibility. For the moment, Zhang Zuolin has largely kept such dissident voices quiet. However Zhang Zuolin, like the pessimists in his camp, understands that this war will be an all or nothing effort - either he succeeds in establishing himself as master of all China, or he will die trying. For Japan, they largely continue to support Marshal Zhang in his war for China, but should he disappoint Tokyo with lack of progress, the Kwantung Army may be provoked into taking drastic action to secure Japan's interests.
When you play the game of thrones, you win or you die.

The Fengtian-Japanese Alliance Victorious?
Although the National Reclamation War threatened to strain the Fengtian - Japanese alliance to the limit, it seems that the war has concluded with Zhang's complete victory. The Kwantung Army is no longer openly scheming to replace Marshal Zhang, and the Tianjin Army has encouraged Zhang to continue his wars of unification.\n\nOnce again, the Fengtian Clique rules in Beijing, and extends its foothold in the Central Plains. However, as Zhang continues to consolidate his authority across the rest of China, many in both Japan and China both wonder if this Sino-Japanese alliance will continue to hold.\n\nTokyo had always hoped for a more subservient partner in China than Zhang, and the Old Marshal has long viewed the Japanese with suspicion and his alliance with them as merely one of convenience. Will Japan and China both continue to maintain their ties despite mutual distrust and conflicts of interest? Or will tensions boil over and Tokyo and Beijing engage in one final war to end all wars?

The Huanggutun Incident
With the National Reclamation War going poorly, it seems that Marshal Zhang's luck has finally run out. Although he had hoped to win the war swiftly, the situation has evolved to become anything but. Zhang's struggles in the war have vindicated the fears of the Kwantung Army, who believe that the Old Marshal may try to negotiate to save his skin, have decided to act decisively.\n\nAs Marshal Zhang was returning to Shenyang after visiting the frontline, his train was hit by a bomb planted by the Kwantung Army. Although Zhang survived for a few hours, the Old Marshal ultimately succumbed to his wounds. Acting immediately, the Kwantung Army has driven out Zhang Xueliang, leaving Fengtian in the hands of Yang Yuting who has reluctantly taken on the position of Generalissimo of the Anguojun.\n\nThe Kwantung Army has largely acted on their own without Tokyo's knowledge or consent, but are gambling on the prospect of total Japanese defeat to force Tokyo's hand. With the Fengtian Government in utter disarray, the Japanese Government will be forced to directly intervene in the National Reclamation War to save Yang's crippled government.
The Manchurian Incident
With the fall of Shenyang, fears have grown among Japanese decision-makers of the possibility of the total loss of Japanese influence in Manchuria - and with it decades of investment and national pride. Zhang Zuolin's incompetent handling of the war and rumours that he is attempting to negotiate a peace behind their backs has led to Kwantung Army hardliners to make a drastic move.\n\nDetonating a small amount of dynamite near a Mantetsu-owned railway (though far away enough that it would not cause any significant damage to the track), they alleged that it was an attack by the Fengtian Clique's enemies on the ostensibly neutral Japanese garrison. Utilising that pretext, the garrison then began shelling Chinese positions - pressuring initially reluctant senior Japanese officers and later Tokyo to embrace the plan.\n\nAs the Japanese moved into position for direct intervention in the conflict, they assassinated Marshal Zhang before he could potentially denounce Japanese imperialism and switch sides. His allies have fled underground and in his place Yang Yuting has assumed control over the remaining Fengtian forces in hopes of preserving some semblance of autonomy for his men.
All eyes are on Marshal Yang to navigate us out of the crisis...

Zhang Cracks Down on Sedition
Zhang Zuolin, though rising from humble circumstances to become master of the Northeast with whatever means available to him, has never been one to tolerate blatant corruption. No, the Grand Marshal has worked tirelessly to promote his regime with an image of inscrutability and moral principle.\n\nMost recently, Marshal Zhang has enacted an anti-corruption purge within his administration, prompting a slew of arrests and executions for those accused of corruption, sedition, and treason. While some have noted Zhang's earnestness in promoting a relatively fair administration, many observers note that most of those purged were tied in some way to Japanese interests operating in Dongbei.\n\nAlthough Marshal Zhang has not publicly revealed the source of bribes, most understand the message he is sending to Tokyo. Japan for their part have not publicly commented on the Old Marshal's recent anti-corruption purges, but the government is undoubtedly displeased with their wayward ally in the Middle Kingdom. However, Tokyo is not in a position to or has deemed it not in their interest to punish Zhang's regime at the moment, leaving the incident largely a victory for Zhang and his Anguojun regime.

Zhang Curtails the Shikan Clique
In the late Qing Dynasty, many sought out a foreign education to learn how they could best heal the ailing Chinese state. Many aspiring soldiers gravitated towards the rising Japanese Empire, which had undertaken a rapid modernisation programme spearheaded by Emperor Meiji. The Japanese for their part encouraged Chinese students to seek an education on their shores, establishing the Tokyo Shinbu Gakko Military Preparatory School, specifically catered towards giving Chinese students military training and education.\n\nWhen the Qing Dynasty was brought down by the Xinhai Revolution and warlords rose up in its place, many of China's prominent generals and leaders were Tokyo Shinbu Gakko alumni. They brought with them a wealth of knowledge on modern warfare, which made them invaluable assets to various powerful warlords. Marshal Zhang recognised the capability of Yang Yuting, who was one such NCO with Japanese education. Yang shared Zhang's ambitions of leading unification efforts, and became a crucial officer within the Fengtian Clique. Yang and other Japanese-educated NCOs formed what became known as the Shikan Clique, and have generally called for ties between Tokyo and Shenyang to be strengthened.\n\nYang's Shikan Clique in recent years has profited greatly from the increase in Japanese influence in Dongbei following Marshal Zhang's retreat from Beijing, and has courted regionalists and disgruntled officers into its camp. The increase in Shikan power has not gone unnoticed under the Old Marshal's watch, as he watches with concern at both the rise of Shikan and Tokyo's influence. Marshal Zhang has increasingly worked to curtail the Shikan Clique's activities, elevating loyalists to higher military positions.
Does Zhang really believe he can unite China without the Shikan Clique?
Concessions to the Concordia Association
In the aftermath of the Anguojun's crippling defeat by Wu Peifu and the Zhili Clique, the Fengtian Clique was once again pushed north of the Great Wall. In this time of vulnerability and weakness, the Russians attempted to pounce on Marshal Zhang's domain, forcing him to rely further on Tokyo's support.\n\nFengtian and Japan stood together against the Russian bear and humiliated the fools like in the days of 1905. In order to consolidate the Sino-Japanese friendship between Marshal Zhang's government and our own, the Concordia Association was formed in Fengtian to promote the ideals of the Pan-Asianist dream. The Association has found a boon of support within Manchuria's ethnic minorities, and has also become the home of certain Japanese radicals who have been expelled from the Home Islands in de facto exile.\n\nRegardless, the Concordia Association remains one of the primary allies of the Shikan Clique and the Kwantung Army, assisting Yang Yuting and his allies whenever possible. While Zhang Zuolin has never truly appreciated the Association, he has been known to shore up temporary support for them in times of strife, such as now.
Marshal Zhang has recognised the wisdom in accepting our aid...
Zhang Empowers Our Advisors
Ever since the Russo-Japanese War which saw our ascendant empire defeat the clumsy Russian Bear, the Kwantung leased territory, which was ours by right ever since the Sino-Japanese War, was returned to us. A year after, the Kwantung Garrison was established, which saw the beginnings of the Kwantung Army. The actual army was established in 1919, when Japan replaced the old governance structure of the port.\n\nSince its creation, the Kwantung Army has maintained influence in the neighbouring Fengtian Clique, and has sought to act as a guiding hand for Japan's influence in Manchuria, and ensure Marshal Zhang's compliance to Tokyo's will. With the Japanese military radicalising substantially in the late 20s, the Kwantung Army for such beliefs, becoming involved in many various coups throughout the interwar period.\n\nThe Kwantung Army stands in staunch rivalry with the Tianjin Army, who look towards the rest of China and hope to assist Zhang Zuolin in destroying the German lapdogs in the Zhili Clique, restore the Anguojun's presence south of the wall, and ensure that Zhang will maintain his ties to Tokyo thereafter, or suffer the consequences. For whatever reasons, Zhang Zuolin has usually attempted to remain aloof from the Kwantung Army's influence, but he has recently brought in some Kwantung Army advisors to assist him in modernising his military force.

Japan Searches for Collaborators
Although Zhang Zuolin is regarded by many in China as the arch-collaborator with Japanese interests thanks to years of Zhili propaganda, the people of the Three Northeastern Provinces understand the true situation. Marshal Zhang was forced to inherit the Japanese as his “allies” upon his takeover of Dongbei, and attempted to contain their influence whilst also not provoking them into taking action.\n\nIt seems that this delicate balancing act is perhaps not long for this world, as it seems that the Empire of Japan is not only unsure of the Old Marshal's ability to win the war, and are even looking for potential replacements. If true, Tokyo could choose from a large array of willing conspirators. Japan's longtime relationship with the Fengtian Clique has produced pro-Japanese elements in all major factions within the government.\n\nThe Concordia Association is already openly pro-Japanese, the Shikan Clique is generally in favour for close ties, the Communications Clique's leaders in Zhang Zongxiang and Lu Zongyu have also shown an openness to working with Tokyo, and even within the Zhang Clique, the Old Marshal's more flexible sworn brothers like Zhang Jinghui and Zhang Haipeng may even be pliable puppets.\n\nAlthough Marshal Zhang is aware of Tokyo's increasing disillusionment with his leadership, there's not much for him to do. He can only recognise the danger he presently is in. The search for collaborators began under local Japanese elements but is now receiving backing from Tokyo itself now, certainly a bad omen for Zhang's government and the fight for a free China.

Japan Reins in Extremists
Although Japan and Fengtian have been allies for two decades, Japan's policy towards us has been incredibly unclear. While Tokyo may decide one thing, the Kwantung Army will do what they have deemed Japan's best interest, as will the Tianjin Army.\n\nWhile the Tianjin Army has generally been more cooperative with the Anguojun, the Kwantung Army not only wants to keep our government contained to north of the Great Wall, and have long disliked Marshal Zhang.\n\nThe increasing radicalism in the Kwantung Army has certainly generated great concern among the Grand Marshal and his inner circle, and years of increasing tensions has certainly been unbeneficial for both powers. Recently, Tokyo has sought to give Marshal Zhang's government some relief by reining in extremist officers stationed in the Northeast, targeted primarily towards the Kwantung Army.\n\nWhile many of their officers have been demoted or recalled, Tianjin Army Officers have been elevated in their place. Tokyo's policy towards Marshal Zhang's government has certainly been made clear, and finally they have enforced the compliance of the wayward armies.

The Japanese Aid Plan
While Fengtian has boasted China's strongest regional economy with most of the nation's heavy industry centred around Fengtian Province and Jilin, the financial situation of the government is no better than the rest of China. Whenever Marshal Zhang has attempted to achieve his ambitions and cross the Great Wall, there have been massive economic consequences back home.\n\nJust a decade ago, the Fengpiao currency collapsed after Zhang's government was unable to secure loans due to the existence of a rival Kuomintang government in Guangzhou, and Zhili resurgence once again relegated Marshal Zhang's government to north of the Great Wall. Recognising the dangers of economic collapse in Fengtian, Tokyo has begun funneling emergency funds to our government through Concordia Association shell organisations.\n\nIn addition to loans, Japan has sent engineers, encouraged its businesses to make contracts with the Fengtian Government, and offered a trade deal for steel. Tokyo's generosity will certainly stabilise the homefront and thus aid the front lines, but every aid package strengthens our economic reliance on Tokyo.
A Faustian Bargain, but one we cannot afford to refuse.
Japanese Sends Arms Shipments
Ever since Marshal Zhang and Tokyo came to a mutually beneficial arrangement, the Fengtian Army has boasted one of the best equipped armies in the Chinese military. During the first Zhifeng War, Wu Peifu's soldiers were dressed in tattered uniforms while the Fengtian Army was fully equipped. To our shame, Wu and his men of rags were able to defeat us.\n\nSince the early 20s, it seems that the various rival warlords have also found friends in high places. Chen Jiongming found friends in the British and Americans, Wu in the Germans, the Kuomintang in France and Russia, and Feng Yuxiang also in Russia. The Fengtian Army has experienced the effects of the modernisation of the armies of the Central Plains firsthand, with equipment attrition skyrocketing.\n\nIn order to resupply our troops in this war for Chinese unification, Japan has sent a massive arms shipment to our government. Of course, Japan has seen to it that sympathetic officers to Tokyo have seen their men resupplied first, and while Anguojun High Command will have a say in weapons distribution, it has not stopped pro-Japanese united being favoured.
We only hope that the cost is not too high...
Japanese Reinforcements Arrive
The increasing chaos in China in recent years has intensified Tokyo's interest in the affairs of our nation, for better or for worse. While Marshal Zhang was able to contain Japanese influence in Dongbei for the first decade of his rule, the collapse of the Fengtian dollar coupled with the loss of Beijing forced previously unseen levels of Japanese influence in the Three Provinces of the Northeast.\n\nWith Marshal Zhang's government once again waging for control of Beijing and China, Tokyo has increased its talons in the Anguojun Government once again. Just yesterday, the government in Tokyo has ordered additional divisions deployed to China in order to shore up its already-stationed Kwantung and Tianjin Armies. Though this move strengthens both of their forces, it in a way weakens both of them, as Tokyo's direct footprint has been increased, now that the Japanese Government is directly involved in this war.
It's all getting away from us...
Unification by Dongbei
Perhaps the greatest ambition of the Old Marshal and his compatriots since the 1920s, the cementing of their control within China has long been a desired dream for many within the Fengtian Clique. With multiple gambits such as the First and Second ZhiFeng Wars, with the latter seeing a term of Fengtian as the beholder of the Beijing Government, their rule was ultimately not to last. Following the Third and Fourth ZhiFeng Wars, Fengtian was ejected to the Three Northeastern Provinces, alongside Rehe.\n\nContinuing to parade themselves as the legitimate successors to the Beiyang Government, the Old Marshal and his subordinates could hardly pose much of a threat in the face of the Zhili's unification of the nation, even when such a foundation was gravely shaken in 1932 and 1933; Zhang Zuolin merely withdrawing from attempted peace negotiations beforehand due to Zhili success in national elections. Yet such a situation was not to last! Rebuilding their strength, in no small part due to Japanese assistance, the army of the Anguojun managed to successfully rout defenders south of the Great Wall, and secure Beijing.\n\nAt the present, there is much jubilation and many celebrations to be held. Both in earnest, and perhaps to mask government difficulties following intense warfare all-throughout the nation-state. Nonetheless, for the third time in the nation's history, Beijing has become the seat of a Dongbei-led government. And for many citizens in China, they look towards the Northeasterners for direction, and for support.
And so our mission is fulfilled.
Fengtian Factionalism Rises
Often thought to be a united force under the strength of a single figure, the Fengtian Clique itself is split into various disparate factions, akin to most major warlord cliques in China. Yet unlike most, it is relatively responsible in its proclamations of internal unity; few would dare defy Marshal Zhang. Even in such an environment however, intense rivalries and inter-personal differences can emerge, most violently and evidently in events such as Guo Songling's rebellion of the 1920s. In-effect, Guo's legacy lives on, shattered and reconstituted both politically and military into two major factions: Shaoshuai, and Shikan.\n\nLed informally by the Young Marshal Zhang Xueliang, the Shaoshuai Clique corresponds to his immediate courtiers, and their ambitions to prop up Guo's reform-minded protégé. As the Old Marshal's de-facto successor, Xueliang has appreciated immense benefits within the Fengtian government, albeit his military and political careers leave much to be desired, so much so as to not mention his social activities.\n\nOn the opposing end lies the Shikan Clique. A group of modernisers, militarists, patriots, and the meritocratic underdogs of Fengtian's factionalism, they are led by the oft misused Yang Yuting, and his close friend Chang Yinhuai. Graduates from the Japanese Army Academy and otherwise, the clique serves as the main vector for internal opposition within the military; fiercely opposed to the seeming nepotism and incompetency of the Shaoshuai, Zhang, Heilongjiang, and other Cliques.\n\nWith the arrival of new glories arrives similarly new difficulties, and the ever simmering lid of Fengtian tensions seems to have finally burst, as whole divisions refuse to heed Central Government orders, and Shikan Clique aficionados meet increasingly with Japanese contacts...
The legacy of Guo Songling...
Failure of Government Economics
Suffice to say, the Chinese economic situation has never been particularly stable ever since the onset of the Warlord Era, perhaps even ever since the decline of the Qing. Industrialisation has usually been at the behest, or at the enquiring, of foreign powers and foreign investments. As such, China's fledgling Feudal land-situation combined with foreign-dominated industrialisation efforts in the urban cities has resulted in quite a tenuous situation throughout the nation.\n\nFurthermore, with the outbreak of hostilities following a brief tenure of relative peace during the Zhilo Unification, investors have fled, industrialists have cordoned their factories and arsenals, and immense damage has been wrought in both the roaring countryside and urban sprawl. In the Northeast, relatively despoiled of damage and conflict, Japanese investments and the clever management of Communications Clique, Zhang Clique, and Recovery League officials have resulted in a flourishing industrial belt stretching through Jilin and other provinces.\n\nDescending from their Northeastern sanctuary however, the Fengtian government has run into all too friendly situation for Chinese Central Governments; an inefficient tax system, local banditry, incompetence and lack of trained officials, and many more issues have resulted in piling debt, and lowering economic productivity. Whilst foreign loans present themselves as a useful bandage to prevent hemorrhaging of national finances, they are but a pittance in light of the true issues. It will undoubtedly take concerted effort to remedy the situation at present.
Best begin searching for loans...
Fears of Fengtian Domination
Politically, Dongbei almost always seemed as a microcosm of broader Chinese currents. Relatively isolated, the Northeastern Cliques had themselves far more concerned with the Japanese to the South, Russians to the North, and the affairs of the Mongol regions to the West. Suffice to say, the provincial governments of the Northeast functioned far more off of personalities and the Fengtian Clique than most other comparable administrations in the era. With relatively little infiltration by organisations south of the Great Wall, namely the Chinese Constitutionalists, Kuomintang, and the Young China Party, various minor Fengtian organisations have managed to rise to prominence: the revived Restoration Society, for example.\n\nYet following the Third and Fourth ZhiFeng Wars, the Northeastern has become a haven for those who have burnt political bridges in the Central Plains and further. Hosting exiled Anhui aficionadoes such as Wang Yitang, Zhang Zuolin's own personal political jockeys such as Pan Fu, or even the Japanophile Communications Clique (far removed from they heyday), the character of the Marshal's rival government has truly been multifaceted, and in-effect tearing at the seams.\n\nAscending from the Great Wall southwards, the character that long loomed Marshal Zhang's government attempts of the 1920s remains large even now. Few would desire to work with Northeasterners, viewed as nothing more but militarists, and perhaps bandits. Uniquely disposed of in-regards to available political muscle, the new Fengtian Government has seemingly brought forth fears of possible domination by men of lesser standing, and even lesser know-how.
Really? As bandits? Still?
A Nation Under the Northeast
Bringing unification to China has been no easy task, and yet it would appear that the consistent, ever-present rival of the Zhili Government has finally emerged on top. Residing within their Northeast sanctuary, and backed by the Japanese, the Fengtian government has finally, for the third time, retaken Beijing. Running through the consequences of national unification, their government has been beset with critical economic shortcomings, and a wasteland of political support; few have forgotten the reputation of Fengtian's aficionados.\n\nFurthermore, it would appear that despite Zhang Zuolin's best efforts, the fracturing Anguojun alliance has begun to tear itself apart. With the ambitions of Tokyo intermixed, a rapidly unfolding tornado of political rivalry and infighting has emerged under the Five Banner flag. The Shikan Clique, the Communications Clique, Recovery League, various democrats and other smaller cliques have all begun to feud over patronage positions and the direction of the government.
$fengtian_endgame_events.004.d.base$\n\nSecuring national unification through the might of the Anguojun, it would appear that the disparate Warlord alliance stewarded by Fengtian's eclectic and corrupt government has begun to mandate proper consolidation under National forces. Whilst perhaps an ideal preferred by a nation so damaged by war and bloodshed for decades, is it tolerable for [ROOT.GetLeader] to submit their government to an intolerable northerner? To permanently sunder any ambitions of their own stake to the presidency?

And yet, many within Yan's camp insist upon his inherent kingmaker role within national politics. With the capacity to descend from Shanxi onto the Central Plain in a lightning strike, the notion of Yan's own Presidential ambitions present themselves as an all-too enticing offer, but is the Model Governor willing to roll the dice? Whatever the case, the time to decide is now, as the Anguojun recoils from its unification and own internal rivalries.

As evident to anyone, knives have been unsheathed, and Governor Zhang owes his loyalty to Marshal Zhang, not to his upstart child or any other member of the Fengtian Clique.

The [FROM.GetAdjective] Rebellion
Following the realisation of Anguojun unification of China, the various cliques and power-holders in China's restored republic have begun to scramble for power and support across the country. Within regionalist sentiment lies a fear of growing government centralisation, corruption within the government ranks (all too well known to the Northeasterners), and a fear of dominance from Dongbei political cliques. With [FROM.GetLeader]'s supporters willing to back their claims with arms, a civil war is likely underway.\n\nThe Central Government of course is expected to have a major advantage, controlling China's major cities and commanding international legitimacy (at least for now) which as given them greater access to loans as well as a larger tax and manpower base to draft an army. The centralised Anguojun however still holds many disloyal regionalists within its ranks. Furthermore, [FROM.GetAdjective] regionalists are confident in the abilities of their forces and expect that others will rise up against the tyrannical dictatorship of the Central Government. And China is no stranger to upsets. What both sides can agree on, however, is that they will not tolerate another warlord era.
$fengtian_endgame_events.005.d.base$\n\n[FROM.GetLeader] and the [FROM.GetRulingParty] have been loosely tied to the Anguojun as of late, with  independent but seemingly compatible roots. Their national ambitions coincided with the Fengtian victory in the North, and rode its wave to unification. Now, however,  with the Central Government attempt to assert its authority over its former allies, it seems that [FROM.GetNameDef] is simply unwilling to accept Dongbei's domination.

Assorted Leaders
Zhang Zuolin
Born to an impoverished family near Shenyang, Zhang Zuolin began his meteoric rise as a bandit exploiting the chaotic military situation of the late Guangxu Era. In the aftermath of the Xinhai Revolution, Zhang was able to secure control of his home province of Fengtian. Zhang's large assortment of alliances, composed of local Beiyang officers and old bandit friends, formed the nucleus of the Fengtian Clique, which would become one of the main Beiyang Clique splinters.\n\nZhang originally made an alliance with Duan Qirui to utilise his Japanese connections for the purpose of securing firearms, but turned on the Anhui Clique alongside the Zhili Clique. The two warlord cliques would later emerge as arch-rivals, a state of affairs still present today. For a time Zhang was the sole controller of Beijing, but the Zhili Clique would restore their control over the city in 1927.\n\nIn the aftermath of the Qing Restoration, Zhang carried out the independence of the Northeast from Beijing's authority and challenged their direct authority to rule China, claiming for himself the mantle of the Xinhai Revolution and rightful heir of the Beiyang Government. Zhang's true commitment to democratic republicanism is dubious at best, but if the Old Marshal can utilise republican rhetoric to restore his status as the internationally recognised government, then so be it.
§YBorn:§! §LMarch 19th, 1875, in Haicheng County, Shengjing District, Great Qing§!\n§YBackground:§! §L$FNG_zhang_zuolin_bio$§!
§YBorn:§! §LMarch 19th, 1875, in Haicheng County, Shengjing District, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §PZhang§!\n§YBackground:§! §L$FNG_zhang_zuolin_bio$§!\n\n§YNotes: Despite his poor literacy and lack of a formal education, the Old Marshal is a capable and self-aware leader with a knack for delegating. His pragmatic nature has many describing him as ideologically 'Pro-Zhang'.§!
Zhang Xueliang
Zhang Xueliang was born into the opposite conditions when compared to his father, the Old Marshal. While Zhang Zuolin was born into poverty and had no formal education, he ensured that his son would be born into a life of privilege and had access to private tutors. Zhang Xueliang would grow up much more open to Western ideas than his conservative father who was disliked by China's intellectual class. Seeking to follow in his father's footsteps, Zhang enrolled in the Fengtian Lecture Hall.\n\nAfter graduating from the artillery department, Zhang Zuolin promoted his son to brigade commander of the guards brigade of the Northeast. When the Fengtian Clique was defeated by the Zhili Clique in the 1st Zhifeng War, Zhang Xueliang was tasked by his father to negotiate a peace. In order to avenge his defeat, Zhang Zuolin began a great modernisation effort in his armies, and Zhang Xueliang was made supervisor of the Northeast Aviation Office, tasked with delivering his father a modern air force which he achieved via the purchase of foreign planes.\n\nThe efforts of the 'Young Marshal' paid off in the 2nd Zhifeng War, which saw the Fengtian Clique secure control of Beijing and dominate Chinese politics.
§YBorn:§! §LJune 3rd, 1901, in Bajiaotai, Shengjing District, Great Qing§!\n§YBackground:§! §L$FNG_zhang_xueliang_desc_body$ While the Zhangs lost Beijing a year later, the Fengtian Clique has once again taken back Beijing, and now stands as the legitimate government of China. Brimming with ambition, only time will tell if the Young Marshal is up to the task of leading the nation.§!
§YBorn:§! §LJune 3rd, 1901, in Bajiaotai, Shengjing District, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §aShaoshuai Clique§!\n§YBackground:§! §L$FNG_zhang_xueliang_desc_body$ Unfortunately for the Zhangs, the Zhili Clique restored their control of Beijing just a few years later. Zhang Xueliang has since been helping his father with further modernisations so that one day, father and son can once again rule the Middle Kingdom.§!\n\n§YNotes: He has been known to frequent the Legation Cities to smoke, gamble, and carousing with women, to his father's dismay. Despite this, Zhang shows a genuine interest in politics, being notably more anti-Japanese than his father.§!
Feng Yong
A dear friend of Zhang Xueliang, having been close since childhood, Feng Yong is the eldest son of Feng Delin who was one of the old veterans of the Fengtian Clique, and an ally of Zhang Zuolin. Sharing the same courtesy name as Xueliang, and growing up together, Feng would accompany Xueliang to the Northeast Army Lecture Hall, and similarly to the Baoding Army Officers School. Serving as a staff officer of the Fengtian Aviation Department, he would play a key role in the establishment of the Northeast Air Force.\n\nFollowing the First ZhiFeng War in 1922, Feng would grow disgusted with the concept of war, resigning from the military and became the general manager of Daye Iron Factory, engaging in armament production, and concurrently principal of Daye Factory Engineer School. In 1926 he donated 3.1 million yuan to establish Feng Yong University, serving as its principal — the first Western style university in the Northeast. With free tuition, and the attaching of great importance to military and physical education, his ideas had considerable effect on the Northeast's students.\n\nFollowing the onset of the Fourth and Fifth ZhiFeng Wars, Feng would emerge out of retirement at the behest of Xueliang, but not to fight the Zhili. Organising his own forces, Feng would focus instead on blunting Japanese operations within Manchuria, allegedly on the Old Marshal's consent.

Whilst not fully committed to the YCP's operation, he is a card carrying member of the party.§!

Ruan Zhenduo
Receiving a standard education, Ruan Zhenduo would graduate from the Japanese styled Nanman Medical College in 1918 after a series of stints in lower educational institutions. Graduating with a medical degree, Ruan would serve as a physician at Fengtian Mantie Hospital, and temporarily served concurrently as a plague prevention physician in Shenyang. From 1919 to 1920, Ruan would study medical chemistry at the School of Medicine in Kyoto Imperial University, and would return to China in 1921 to serve as a school official, and school physician at Northeastern University.\n\nServing as a doctor up until 1924, he would become president of the Fengtian branch of the All-China Medical Association, and in 1928 would be appointed as the Assistant Officer for Plague Prevention. In 1930, Ruan would serve as director of the Changchun Ji-Chang Ji-Dun Railway Hospital, and in the following year he would be appointed as the consultant of the Fengtian Local Maintenance Association.\n\nShooting into politics utilising Japanese contacts, Ruan would be appointed as Secretary-General of the Fengtian Provincial Government, and would establish the Concordia Association, with others from the Manchuria Youth League, in order to be the facet by which Japan influences Fengtian's Assembly. Continuing to dutifully display his expertise in a series of transportaion and communication positions, Ruan would continue to champion the cause of Japan in the rump assembly.

Yang Yuting

Wang Yitang
§YBorn:§! §L1878, in Hefei County, Anhui Province, Great Qing§!\n§YBackground:§! §L$FNG_wang_yitang_desc_body$ Now entrusted with stewardship of China, many believe that Wang's ascendance to the presidency is the sign that Anhui's gambit played of.§!

Passing the Imperial Examination in 1904, Wang Yitang would request the Qing Court to allow him to study military affairs in Japan, being sent to the Tokyo Shinbu Gakko. Travelling to Russia in 1909 on diplomatic business, Wang would receive the Order of the Precious Star from the Tsar, and would tour a series of European and American countries to investigate military, political and transportation developments. Travelling back home once again, he would serve as General Manager of the Jilin Military Prep Department.\n\nJoining a series of Republican parties in the aftermath of Xinhai, Wang would be elected to the first Senate, joining Li Yuanhong's Republican Party, later merging into the Progressive Party. Serving in Yuan Shikai's Constitutional Conference on behalf of Anhui, Wang would support Yuan Shikai's monarchy ambitions, and after its failure would join Duan Qirui's Anhui Clique.\n\nHaving a tenure as Speaker of the Senate, Wang would organise the Anfu Club Party-State, effectively ruling China through a clique within a clique. Forced to flee to Japan following an arrest warrent after the fall of Anhui, Wang would participate in Duan's 1924 Government under Zhang Zuolin, becoming a vocal proponent and major figure. Zhang Zongxiang
§YBorn:§! §L1879, in Wuxing County, Zhejiang Province, Great Qing§!\n§YBackground:§! §L$FNG_zhang_zongxiang_desc_body$§! Now President of a Pro-Japanese Republic, few look upon their fellow countryman with anything but animosity.
§YBorn:§! §L1879, in Wuxing County, Zhejiang Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §cNew Communications Clique§!\n§YBackground:§! §L$FNG_zhang_zongxiang_desc_body$§!
Passing the imperial examination at a young age, Zhang Zongxiang would begin his long and storied history with Japanese culture by travelling there in 1899, where he studied at the First Higher School, and the Law Department of the Tokyo Imperial University, and later Meiji University. Returning to China in 1903, he would teach at the Imperial University of Beijing, becoming a Jinshi in the Court. Serving in various ministries, he would even participate in the trial of the attempted assassination of Regent Zaifeng.\n\nSent by Yuan Shikai to participate in the North-South peace talks with Tang Shaoyi in 1911, Zhang would continue his work in Yuan's employ, becoming Minister of Justice in 1914. In 1916 he became Minister to Japan, colluding with the New Communication's Clique to secretly negotiate a dubiously beneficial deal in regards to Chinese debts to Japan. In 1918 he would sign three loans to Japan totalling 60 million yen, giving the Japanese railway and mineral rights, alongside acceding occupation of Jinan and Qingdao to Japan.\n\nRepresenting Beiyang at the Weltkrieg's Spa Peace Conference, news would break out of his Pro-Japan dealings, and he would be denounced, beaten, expelled from his hometown, and forced from his position in the government. In 1920 he would serve as the general manager of the joint Sino-Japanese Bank, and in 1925 as general manager of the Beijing Commercial Bank. In 1928 he would briefly move to Qingdao, before being recalled by his old friends Lu and Cao to join their revived New Communications Clique in Fengtian.
Lu Zongyu
§YBorn:§! §L1876, in Hangzhou Prefecture, Zhejiang Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §cNew Communications Clique§!\n§YBackground:§! §LBorn into a merchant family, Lu Zongyu would enter Nanjing Wenzheng Academy, and in 1899 would study at Waseda University in Law and Economics, at his own expense. In 1902 he returned to China and worked as a tax administrator in Beijing, before teaching at the Jinshi and Police Academy. In 1905, Lu would become Director of the Patrol Police under Xu Shichang, and would later serve as Counselor to Aisin-Gioro Zaize, Minister of Political Affairs.\n\nAccompanying Xu Shichang to serve as General Manager of the Fengtian Foreign Affairs Bureau, Lu would follow Xu back to Beijing in 1908, and in 1910 was a member of the Council of State. An assistant manager in the Bank of Communications, he would soon become acting vice-minister of Finance. In 1913 he was a member of the Senate, and became Chinese minister to Japan that same year.\n\nConveying China's neutral position to Japan's occupation of Shandong, Lu would be at the forefront of Japan's Twenty One Demands, and with Yuan's death, Lu would be recalled. Becoming Chairman of the Board of the Bank of Communications, Lu would be sent by Cao Rulin to negotiate the Nishihara Loan with Zhang Zongxiang, and in 1917 would become general manager of the joint Sino-Japanese bank. In 1919 he would form the New Communications Clique with Cao, but that same year would be beat by protestors alongside Zhang, and dismissed. Serving in the Senate in 1925, Lu would ultimately live in Tianjin, before being called by Cao to join him in Fengtian.§!
Kita Seiichi
